{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:43","updatedTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:43","title":"Ben & Jerry's maker Unilever is offering a 4-day working week at full pay to its New Zealand staff — and all its 150,000 worldwide employees could be next","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/4-day-working-week-unilever-full-pay-new-zealand-2020-12","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9196432121130018740221?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Ben &#38; Jerry&#39;s\" height=\"2847\" width=\"3797\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Newscast/Universal Images Group via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Unilever is offering its New Zealand staff a four-day working week at their normal full pay.</li>\n<li>The year-long trial will give employees flexibility in their work-life balance and make the company more productive, Unilever said.</li>\n<li>New Zealand's prime minister Jacinda Ardern has supported a four-day week, saying it would be good for domestic tourism.</li>\n<li>The success of the Unilever trial could determine whether the company rolls it out to its 150,000 global employees.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><section><p>Consumer goods giant Unilever is offering all 81 of its New Zealand workers a four-day week – and they don't have to take a pay cut.</p><p>Staff will retain their full salaries while working 80% of their usual contracted hours. The new structure will give them more flexibility to decide when and how they work best, Unilever said in a <a href=\"https://www.unilever.com.au/news/press-releases/2020/unilever-nz-to-trial-four-day-work-week-at-full-pay.html\">press release Tuesday</a>.</p><p>The trial starts December 7 and will last a year.</p><p>Unilever is behind brands including Ben &#38; Jerry's, Magnum, and Vaseline.</p><p>The move will improve employees' mental and physical wellbeing, Nick Bangs, the company's New Zealand managing director, said.</p><p>It will also make the company more productive, he added.</p></section><section><p>\"Our goal is to measure performance on output, not time,\" Bangs said. \"We believe the old ways of working are outdated and no longer fit for purpose.\"</p><p>The growing momentum for a four-day working is \"validation of the catalytic role COVID-19 has played in shaking up standard working practices,\" he said.</p><p>The country's prime minister&#160;Jacinda Ardern&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/new-zealand-jacinda-ardern-four-day-workweek-help-economy-tourism-2020-5\">has been one of the driving forces behind a four-day working week</a>, saying it could boost domestic tourism as well as aid New Zealand's recovery from COVID-19.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/inside-unilevers-plan-to-grow-plant-based-food-sales-2020-11?r=gd-sub\">A Unilever exec reveals how the company will reach $1.1B in plant based sales by 2027</a></em></p><p>Unilever drew inspiration from New Zealand estate planning firm Perpetual Guardian, which rolled out a four-day week to all its 240 staff in 2018.</p><p>Unilever will share the trial's outcomes with other New Zealand businesses, and said it hopes they will reflect on&#160;their own ways of working.</p></section><section><p>The current trial is only for New Zealand staff, but Unilever said the trial could determine whether the company looks into rolling out the initiative to its 150,000 employees globally.</p></section><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article factory activity grew at its quickest rate in a decade in November, as the economic recovery led to manufacturing firms processing higher volumes and recording an improvement in new orders, according to <a href=\"https://www.markiteconomics.com/Public/Home/PressRelease/97a7429689ba4d94b649ec9ce93c04e5\">data released</a> Tuesday.</p><p>Manufacturing companies posted the strongest improvement in overall activity a decade, rising for a seventh month in a row. The Caixin China General Purchasing Managers Index (PMI) rose to 54.9 in November from 53.6 last month.</p><p>PMI survey data is widely used to track business trends across the world's biggest economies. A reading of 50 separates expansion from contraction.&#160;</p><p>A breakdown of the report showed manufacturing sector employment rose at its fastest pace since May 2011, while measures of demand showed domestic consumption was the engine of growth last month, rather than exports. Some of China's main importing customers, such as the United States and the eurozone, continue to struggle with the economic fallout of the pandemic, which has undermined consumer and producer demand.</p><p><strong><em>Read More: </em></strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-cheap-value-emerging-markets-dave-grecsek-2020-11\"><em>Cheap stocks just had their best month ever. Higher demand for input materials led to a rise in costs, and in turn, companies raised their own selling prices.</p><p>Positive data from China shows that it is the first economy to successfully emerge from the COVID-19 pandemic with not only fewer deaths and cases of the virus, but also with a robust recovery.</p><p>Equity investors took heart from the data, pushing China's <a class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><a href=\"https://www.dreamersdoers.me/\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"e6c95ebd04558e0dbff6aecd80881814\">Dreamers href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>As most founders have experienced, entrepreneurial journeys are anything but linear. There are ideas that propel you forward, setbacks that challenge you, and pivots that have you starting from what feels like scratch.&#160;</p><p>Yet despite the inevitable trial and error companies are bound to face, there is usually one moment — an aha moment — where the pieces seem to perfectly align and the vision becomes clear. While the path still isn't easy, having that North Star to refer to can be essential when a company is still just a glimmer of an idea.</p><p>For these 20 female founders, there was a clear aha moment when they knew it was time to go all-in with their company. Whether that moment came out of a personal need, a lifelong passion, or a glaring problem that needed to be solved, their stories beautifully illustrate the significance of having one moment where it all clicks, ultimately igniting their passions to make their dreams a reality.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/millennial-cofounders-feminine-care-startup-blume-raised-millions-one-month\">How the millennial cofounders of feminine-care company Blume raised $3.3 million in funding in just one month</a></em></p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\t1. Tiffany Yu\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc4143e037cbd0018612c6f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tiffany Yu\" height=\"577\" width=\"768\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tiffany Yu.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tiffany Yu</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Founder and CEO of </em></strong><a href=\"http://mydiversability.com\"><strong><em>Diversability</em></strong></a><strong><em>, an award-winning social enterprise to rebrand disability through the power of community.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> I started Diversability because it was something I needed for myself. As someone who acquired a disability as a result of a tragic car accident, I desperately wanted to root myself in community and talk about my story in a more empowering way.</p><p>At the time, I couldn't find other organizations that were cross-disability, that included non-disabled people in the conversation, and that celebrated disability in an empowering way that was rooted in pride, identity, and culture. Thanks to support from the Dreamers &#38; Doers community, I worked on Diversability as a side hustle before transitioning into it full-time.&#160;</p><p>I truly believe that the best ideas come from looking at ourselves as the first customer; in other words, what are the pain points in our own customer journey that we can solve? Chances are, it may help others too.</p><p>&#160;</p>\n\t2. Rahama Wright\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc4148f037cbd0018612c71?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Rahama Wright\" height=\"1332\" width=\"1776\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Rahama Wright.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Rahama Wright</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Founder and CEO of </em></strong><a href=\"https://sheayeleen.com/\"><strong><em>Shea Yeleen</em></strong></a><strong><em>, a DC-based social impact beauty business that creates shea butter body care products that generate living wages for women in Ghana.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> Following my Peace Corps service, I made the ambitious decision to launch Shea Yeleen, a social impact company that creates living wage jobs for women-owned shea butter cooperatives in Ghana. I was in my early 20s with very little business experience, but I was inspired by the hardworking women who are the backbone of the global shea butter supply chain. I'm a first generation Ghanaian-American, so the lives of women in rural Ghana reflect the life of my mother, who immigrated to the US in the 1980s to give her kids a better future.&#160;</p><p>Every day, through my business, I challenge the societal limitations put on African women by connecting the producers of this amazing skin care product directly to our customers. Through ethically sourcing shea butter, cooperative members have the financial resources to invest in household needs, education for their kids, and other income-generating activities. Shea Yeleen is proof that women, when given access to the right opportunities, can become respected leaders in their families and their communities.</p>\n\t3. Shivani Honwad\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc414f2037cbd0018612c72?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Shivani Honwad\" height=\"375\" width=\"500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Shivani Honwad.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Shivani Honwad</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Founder and principal attorney of </em></strong><a href=\"http://www.shivanilaw.com/\"><strong><em>The Law Firm of Shivani Honwad</em></strong></a><strong><em> LLC, which specializes in immigration and business legal matters.&#160;</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> One of the main reasons I decided to start my own law firm was to help educate and empower female entrepreneurs. Many women repeatedly told me how they felt intimidated by the legal process or hesitant to approach a lawyer out of fear, so they were routinely taken advantage of as they sought to build their companies &#8212; losing money and/or their products or designs.</p><p>By having more of a client-centric focus, not only do I help my clients understand their legal options and draft and file documents as necessary, but I also work to empower them to stick up for themselves and negotiate for better business deals. Helping people turn their dreams into reality is one of my favorite things to do.&#160;</p>\n\t4. Xi Chen\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc415a7037cbd0018612c75?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Xi Chen\" height=\"1499\" width=\"1999\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Xi Chen.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Xi Chen</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Owner and creative director of </em></strong><a href=\"https://sonderlier.com/\"><strong><em>Sonderlier</em></strong></a><strong><em>, which designs effortlessly chic clothes that are as comfortable as your favorite sweats.&#160;</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> I founded Sonderlier to liberate women from having to choose between comfort and confidence. I had a daily struggle with beautiful clothes that never left my closet versus comfy clothes that made me feel frumpy. And I realized this is a struggle shared by many other women. Frustrated by existing options, I decided to create my own designs. By approaching clothing design with the angle of wellness and self love, I hope to help women feel beautiful and be their most elevated selves every day.</p>\n\t5. Fernanda Dobal\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc415ea037cbd0018612c77?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Fernanda Dobal\" height=\"1332\" width=\"1776\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Fernanda Dobal.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Fernanda Dobal</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Cofounder of </em></strong><a href=\"http://bia.care\"><strong><em>Bia.Care</em></strong></a><strong><em>, which supports women going through menopause so they can manage their symptoms and go back to doing the things they love.&#160;</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> I've always worked in social impact tech and as a designer, I see design as a powerful tool to change the world. I love building things. Starting a company, for me, is an opportunity to make an impact: by creating company culture and a shared mission among my team, and also by bringing something new and positive to solve a problem in the world.&#160;</p>\n\t6. Rana Good\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc4167450e71a0011557dcf?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Rana Good\" height=\"1332\" width=\"1776\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Rana Good.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Rana Good</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Founder of </em></strong><a href=\"https://nairanyc.com/\"><strong><em>Na&#239;ra NYC</em></strong></a><strong><em>, an editorial platform for women of color which will launch products in the near future.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> The absence of women of color in the media made me spring into action. I've been a journalist for a decade writing for publications like Forbes, Travel + Leisure, Men's Journal, and more. I realized there was no publication catering specifically to women of color and wanted to build an editorial platform that would represent us and tell our stories. In the future we will launch products in our categories (beauty, travel, style, and culture) that will also cater specifically to our audience to further fill a void.</p>\n\t7. Melissa Perri\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc416eb037cbd0018612c7c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Melissa Perri\" height=\"1499\" width=\"1999\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Melissa Perri.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Melissa Perri</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>CEO of </em></strong><a href=\"http://produxlabs.com\"><strong><em>Produx Labs</em></strong></a><strong><em>, a three-pronged solution to all things product management with the Product Institute, CPO Accelerator, and Produx Labs consultancy.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> I started my first company in a startup accelerator in Italy, not because I had a great idea, but because I wanted to start a company. That failed before it even got off the ground.&#160;</p><p>While I was figuring out what to do next, I kept receiving calls from former coworkers asking me to come in and teach their companies how to do product management. I saw more and more companies struggling with how to do product well. I soon realized that this was a problem worth starting a company to solve. There was a problem in the market, and I knew how to solve it. Produx Labs was born six years ago, and now we're a team of over 15 people, with consulting services and online education.</p>\n\t8. Jiyoon Cha\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc4176f037cbd0018612c7d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Jiyoon Cha\" height=\"562\" width=\"749\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Jiyoon Cha.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jiyoon Cha</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Art director of </em></strong><a href=\"https://jiyooncha.com/\"><strong><em>Jiyoon Cha Studio</em></strong></a><strong><em>, a creative studio focused on branding, art direction, and creative services.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment': </strong>I started my own creative practice to lead through my own creative process and expression and to grow with my clients. Currently, I work at Scout Lab as an art director and design lead, which has given me a sense of community through collaborating with my talented coworkers and learning from them. During my personal time, my focus has shifted towards a sustainable lifestyle and helping shape the creative industry with innovative and sustainable ways to move forward as my lifelong passion and journey.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-women-leading-making-big-money-zero-waste-movement\">3 women leading the zero-waste movement reveal how they're managing to change the world while making a profit</a></em></p>\n\t9. Jessica Kelly\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc41804037cbd0018612c7f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Jessica Kelly\" height=\"1332\" width=\"1777\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Jessica Kelly.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jessica Kelly</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Founder and CEO of </em></strong><a href=\"http://www.thr3efold.com\"><strong><em>THR3EFOLD</em></strong></a><strong><em>, a tech platform for brands to find ethical factories and learn how to build their business for people, planet, and profit.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> I knew I loved the fashion industry, but I hit a wall where I was craving more meaning in my career. Getting free product placed on celebrities or panicking over a button emergency wasn't curing cancer.&#160;</p><p>On a life-changing trip to Africa, I was deeply impacted by the joyful, generous, hardworking people of Zimbabwe, but I was saddened by how little job opportunity there was for them to provide for their families. That set me on a mission to find a way to use fashion to create sustainable employment around the world, and now that is what we do by helping apparel and accessory brands find ethical factories for their manufacturing.</p><p>By shifting the supply chain in an ethical direction, we can grow those factories, and in turn grow dignified, sustainable job opportunities. I believe it is possible to create a 100% ethically-made fashion industry, and that is what drives me every day.</p>\n\t10. Samantha Patil\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc41925037cbd0018612c82?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Samantha Patil\" height=\"1126\" width=\"1500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Samantha Patil.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Samantha Patil</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Cofounder and CEO of </em></strong><a href=\"https://www.welltraveledclub.com\"><strong><em>Well Traveled</em></strong></a><strong><em>, the first members-only travel platform designed for today's modern traveler, with a unique approach built on trust, community, and connection.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> Like many entrepreneurs, the idea for Well Traveled was born out of a personal pain point. I travel often, and while I love experiencing new places and cultures, I've found that trip planning is time-consuming and frustrating. Finding relevant, trustworthy recommendations is especially challenging. And I just thought, why is this process so broken? Travel planning should be a positive experience: you're getting ready to do something exciting!&#160;</p><p>After doing some research, I realized the current solutions are failing to meet the needs of today's modern traveler. I saw a gap in the market and the opportunity to build something better, so I decided to do something about it.</p>\n\t11. Lyda Mclallen\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc4197250e71a0011557dd3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Lyda Mclallen\" height=\"820\" width=\"1094\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Lyda Mclallen.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lyda Mclallen</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Founder of </em></strong><a href=\"https://talkplustell.com/\"><strong><em>Talk+Tell</em></strong></a><strong><em>, which self-publishes profitable books that readers love.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> It happened really organically. My passion over the last decade has always been reading and helping authors share their stories with readers and people. I find that both fiction and nonfiction stories create positive change and a deeper understanding of our reality. A lot of our reality is shaped by the stories we read, from books to news articles to a friend's Facebook posts.</p><p>Stories in all of their forms are inspirational and can generate change. Throughout my career, authors kept following me online and asking for advice. Slowly I built up a following and decided to make the leap and start my own self-publishing company. I love what I do! My favorite part is helping authors develop their story into a book that sells, and I love hearing where their inspiration came from.</p><p>&#160;</p>\n\t12. Sara Banks\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc419ec037cbd0018612c84?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Sara Banks\" height=\"768\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Sara Banks.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Sara Banks</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Founder and CEO of </em></strong><a href=\"https://steamlineluggage.com/\"><strong><em>SteamLine Luggage</em></strong></a><strong><em>, a vintage-inspired luggage brand with modern amenities, creating timeless pieces that elevate the travel experience and home d&#233;cor.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> I founded SteamLine Luggage when in 2008 I saw a desperate need for beautiful luggage. Luggages is our largest seen travel accessory, and I wanted to create elegant luggage that brought glamour back to modern-day travel. Packing gorgeous suitcases helps excite the start of an adventure, and they bring joy along the way! They are ideal for sightly storage in the home when not being used for exploring.&#160;</p>\n\t13. Shabrina Koeswologito\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc41a2d037cbd0018612c85?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Shabrina Koeswologito\" height=\"266\" width=\"354\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Shabrina Koeswologito.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Shabrina Koeswologito</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Founder of </em></strong><a href=\"https://www.sheglimmr.com\"><strong><em>Glimmr</em></strong></a><strong><em>, a mix between a news app and podcast company that aims to empower women of Indonesia to become their best selves.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> For Indonesian women, to speak up and challenge the norm is not typical. Interestingly, Indonesia has seen growth in female-led businesses. Out of 60 million small-to-medium businesses in Indonesia, about 14 million were founded by women in 2019.&#160;</p><p>I kept pushing to make my dream happen. After about four years, I finally got a chance to finish my graduate degree and work in New York City. There I found like-minded females who weren't afraid or ashamed of pursuing their goals. Even though I started my life from zero, the 3.5 years of experience equal 10 years of knowledge at home. Right now I'm back in Indonesia, because I want to give back to other Indonesian women by helping them become the best version of themselves and achieve freedom &#8212; financial and/or speaking up &#8212; faster. I believe that having more women change-makers can contribute to the economy. It can give them the confidence to start something again.</p>\n\t14. Tiffany Pham\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc41aaf037cbd0018612c86?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tiffany Pham\" height=\"999\" width=\"1332\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tiffany Pham.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tiffany Pham</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Founder and CEO of </em></strong><a href=\"https://onmogul.com/\"><strong><em>Mogul</em></strong></a><strong><em>, the largest platform for women and diverse professionals.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> My first \"aha\" moment was after my grandmother passed away when I was 14. My grandmother was an amazing mogul of her time. She ran businesses across multiple industries in Asia and provided others in need with opportunities and resources. I wanted to be like her, and I made a promise to her that I would follow in her footsteps. I envisioned building a platform that would help people grow to their greatest potential.&#160;</p><p>The second \"aha\" moment came when several magazines had written about my unique and unusual jobs. My email address was available online, and I woke up to a flooded inbox from so many young women and men from around the world asking for help, advice, and what resources I was accessing to receive these opportunities at such a young age. I started sharing this information one on one. That's when I realized what if we could have a platform where millions of people could share obstacles, challenges, ideas, insights, and opportunities to help each other become the best versions of ourselves. I then taught myself how to code and created the first version of Mogul.&#160;</p>\n\t15. Olivia Bowser\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc41c10037cbd0018612c89?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Olivia Bowser\" height=\"996\" width=\"1329\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Olivia Bowser.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Olivia Bowser</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Founder and CEO of </em></strong><a href=\"https://www.liberatestudio.com/\"><strong><em>Liberate</em></strong></a><strong><em>, a new kind of wellness studio with an emphasis on mental health.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> A catch-up with friends turned into a deeper discussion about our broader circles and the struggles we're all experiencing. We shared stories of friends overly stressed at work, feeling lonely, or dealing with severe anxiety or depression. I heard the same narrative over and over again &#8212; we feel stuck and alone.</p><p>The biggest takeaway was that most of our friends heavily invested in their physical health to give them a temporary release, but that same investment wasn't going towards their mental health. As someone who practices solo meditation to deal with anxiety, I realized there wasn't a place where mental health, physical movement, and community worked together as one. I needed to create that space.</p>\n\t16. Teresa Comi\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc41d2a50e71a0011557ddb?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Teresa Comi\" height=\"1109\" width=\"1479\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Teresa Comi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Teresa Comi</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Founder and innovation strategist of </em></strong><a href=\"https://www.teresacomi.com\"><strong><em>Teresa Comi</em></strong></a><strong><em>, which guides companies in the cultural, design, and wellness space to create better products, services, and experiences, and cofounder and CMO of </em></strong><a href=\"http://www.caelideco.com\"><strong><em>Caeli</em></strong></a><strong><em>, an ethical home decoration brand with the mission to create inspired and relaxed homes.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> My first company was a passion project that I cofounded after a long trip to India. I had always loved interior design, and in India I discovered the beauty and authenticity of their crafts, so my dream was to share them with the world in an ethical way. I honestly believe that a better world starts in a slow home! Caeli was spontaneous and passion-driven, but I learned a lot about starting a business that I could use for a second business, an innovation consultancy firm. I founded my second business because I wanted to create my own path. Having worked in Fortune 500 companies, I always felt like I was walking someone else's road, so I decided to take control and build the road my way.&#160;</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/women-in-venture-capital-break-glass-ceiling\">Less than 10% of decision makers in venture capital are women. Here's a managing partner's advice for shattering the glass ceiling.</a></em></p>\n\t17. Wendy Wecksell\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc41d6950e71a0011557ddc?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Wendy Wecksell\" height=\"1499\" width=\"1999\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Wendy Wecksell.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Wendy Wecksell</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Founder of </em></strong><a href=\"https://www.wxlpartners.com/\"><strong><em>WxL Partners</em></strong></a><strong><em>, which empowers women in their careers by empowering them in their relationships.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> I had zero desire to start something myself, but I cared about championing good and talented people I believe in. What I saw in myself as the CEO of a girls' self-organization was that I ironically had the lowest self-worth that year. It was also not the professional skills that got in the way of my and the organization's success; it was my personal beliefs, patterns, and habits. I saw this same personal limitation in the founders and leaders I believed in as well, so I knew I had to make the thing that wasn't my job, my job. I wanted to tackle the root of the problem, and so WxL was born.</p>\n\t18. Nikki Goldman\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc41f4150e71a0011557ddf?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Nikki Goldman\" height=\"1384\" width=\"1846\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Nikki Goldman.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Nikki Goldman</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>CEO of </em></strong><a href=\"https://www.iocoaching.co/\"><strong><em>I/O Coaching</em></strong></a><strong><em>, which helps to develop world-class leaders through coaching and training programs.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> Growing up in startups, whenever you questioned employee turnover, the line \"this % employee churn is normal at companies our size\" was the standard answer. Those churn numbers were HIGH! I constantly questioned it. How was it that we spent so much time and money recruiting candidates that we were so excited about, but six to 12 months later, voluntarily or involuntarily, they were leaving the company? What a waste!&#160;</p><p>I thought that there must be something we can do to make people more successful at these fast-moving, innovative, challenging companies. That's why I started I/O Coaching. My goal with I/O Coaching is to put the onus to ensure that employees thrive back on the company. I believe it's the employers' job to invest in their people to optimize for their success. We now partner with forward-thinking companies to do just that, and in turn, reduce their churn.</p>\n\t19. Jes Osrow\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc41fe750e71a0011557de0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Jes Osrow\" height=\"1001\" width=\"1333\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Jes Osrow.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jes Osrow</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Cofounder and DEIBA specialist of </em></strong><a href=\"http://www.therisejourney.com\"><strong><em>The Rise Journey</em></strong></a><strong><em>, which helps companies build their best team and a powerful organizational culture.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> My business partner and I both took a mini masterclass in D&#38;I because we recognized that the status quo was majorly messed up. I wanted to create the business that I'd be proud to work for, to hire for, and most importantly, a business that was ready to stand by their values while helping other organizations live through theirs. I wanted to be as transparent in business as I am in life while making an impact on the world &#8212; one business at a time. If you can't take action to change the world and help others do the same, then what's the point?</p>\n\t20. Trisha Okubo\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc4206a50e71a0011557de2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Trisha Okubo\" height=\"768\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Trisha Okubo.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Trisha Okubo</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><em>Founder and creative director of </em></strong><a href=\"https://www.maisonmiru.com\"><strong><em>Maison Miru Jewelry</em></strong></a><strong><em>, which helps express creativity through accessible jewelry: modern heirlooms to tell unique stories.</em></strong></p><p><strong>My 'aha moment':</strong> If there's something that needs to exist in the world but doesn't, it's up to you to create it. On the surface, Maison Miru Jewelry is a tiny but mighty company that helps you express your creativity through accessible jewelry: modern heirlooms that you can mix and match to tell your own story. But our bigger goal is to inspire creative thinking to make the world a better, more just place &#8212; specifically through supporting fellow creative entrepreneurs. Our long-term goal is to serve as a platform for creative entrepreneurship as we share our learnings with fellow entrepreneurs, especially women and minorities, to amplify our impact.</p>\n</div><div Payne)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5fc62c86037cbd00186130a8?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn68@2020_4/2020/12/01/14-28-08-590_52f7e14c968a5ac7.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn19@2020_6/2020/12/01/14-28-10-417_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=fMRakeLb6to:zfxrFLhW9sM:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn75@2020_6/2020/12/01/14-28-11-603_7c73655a0be4d4ec.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=fMRakeLb6to:zfxrFLhW9sM:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn12@2020_3/2020/12/01/14-28-05-977_8c409069e6182d3a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn100@2020_6/2020/12/01/14-28-08-006_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=fMRakeLb6to:zfxrFLhW9sM:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn76@2020_6/2020/12/01/14-28-06-363_c6981244fc4a4312.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/fMRakeLb6to":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn92@2020_3/2020/12/01/14-28-10-941_0b29d780632935ea.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1606832863094},{"createdTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:43","updatedTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:43","title":"The rise and fall of White House COVID-19 advisor Dr. Scott Atlas, a lockdown skeptic who had Trump's ear and fought with experts like Fauci","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/scott-atlas-new-medical-adviser-anti-lockdown-pro-schools-reopening-2020-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f72fad90ab50d00184ace8c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"scott atlas donald trump\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Dr. Scott Atlas speaks at White House press conference on September 23, 2020, as President Donald Trump looks on.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/president-donald-trump-listens-to-white-house-coronavirus-news-photo/1228675819?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">MANDEL NGAN/AFP via Getty</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Dr. Scott Atlas resigned from the White House coronavirus task force on Monday, after less than four months on the team.&#160;</li>\n<li>President Donald Trump brought Atlas onto the task force in August, after he had appeared on Fox News for months, echoing the president's anti-lockdown opinions.&#160;</li>\n<li>Atlas is a healthcare-policy expert who works at the Hoover Institute, a conservative think tank at Stanford University. He is not an infectious-disease expert.</li>\n<li>Yet according to reports, Trump sidelined <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-barely-meets-white-house-coronavirus-task-force-francis-collins-2020-10\">other public-health experts</a> while hearing Atlas' advice.</li>\n<li>Atlas also worried <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/scott-atlas-hits-back-critics-questioning-science-fauci-redfield-2020-10\">top US health experts</a>: the CDC's director was <a href=\"https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/politics-news/redfield-voices-alarm-over-influence-trump-s-new-coronavirus-task-n1241221\">overheard saying</a> \"everything\" Atlas says \"is false,\" and Dr. Anthony Fauci <a href=\"https://edition.cnn.com/world/live-news/coronavirus-pandemic-09-28-20-intl/h_c19249ebeb35a18392b10e42b34827ac\">said he was concerned</a> that Atlas was giving \"incorrect\" information to the president.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Dr. Scott Atlas, President Donald Trump's anti-lockdown coronavirus advisor, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/scott-atlas-reportedly-resigned-from-white-coronavirus-task-force-2020-11\">resigned on Monday</a>, after months of stirring up controversy.&#160;</p><p>Atlas was bought onto the White House coronavirus task force in August, as a <a href=\"https://www2.oge.gov/Web/oge.nsf/Resources/Special+Government+Employees#:~:text=As%20defined%20in%2018%20U.S.C.,period%20of%20365%20consecutive%20days.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">special government employee</a>, meaning his role in the task force was temporary and would not exceed 130 days. <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/politics/dr-scott-atlas-resigns-special-adviser-trump-coronavirus\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Fox News</a> reported that his tenure was set to expire next week.&#160;</p><p>The White House confirmed Atlas' resignation but declined to comment further.</p><p>In a resignation letter cited by Fox News, Atlas said his \"advice was always focused on minimizing all the harms from both the pandemic and the structural policies themselves, especially to the working class and the poor.\"</p><p>But many people in the scientific community were skeptical of Atlas' intentions during his time working for the president, with reports saying he was pushing a \"herd immunity\" strategy that experts believe would have led to an unnecessary loss of lives.&#160;</p><h2>Spotted on Fox News</h2><p>Atlas was brought onto Trump's coronavirus task force in August, after appearing on Fox News for several months, where he often echoed the president's views — including an opposition to lockdowns.</p><p>He is a senior fellow at the Hoover Institution, a conservative think tank at Stanford University. Unlike some other experts on the task force, he did not have a specialty in either infectious diseases or public health. Instead, he focuses on healthcare policy and has a <a href=\"https://profiles.stanford.edu/scott-atlas?tab=bio\">background in neuroradiology</a>, which is the reading of X-rays, CT scans, and MRIs.</p><p>Nonetheless, Atlas became a favorite of the president. National Institutes of Health director and White House task force member Dr. Francis Collins <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/sections/coronavirus-live-updates/2020/10/20/925790239/nih-director-guardedly-optimistic-about-vaccine-approval-by-end-of-2020\">told NPR</a> on October 20 that Trump had not attended task force meetings \"for quite some time,\" <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-barely-meets-white-house-coronavirus-task-force-francis-collins-2020-10\">and is only hearing from Atlas and Vice President Mike Pence instead</a>.</p><p>In October, <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/trumps-den-of-dissent-inside-the-white-house-task-force-as-coronavirus-surges/2020/10/19/7ff8ee6a-0a6e-11eb-859b-f9c27abe638d_story.html\">The Washington Post</a> also reported that the Trump administration was <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-hasnt-spent-9-billion-earmarked-for-coronavirus-testing-report-2020-10\">\"sitting\" on $9 billion earmarked for COVID-19 testing</a> because Atlas was opposed to expanding the testing regime.</p><h2>The medical community's red flags</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f72fb9574fe5b0018a8de0e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"robert redfield\" height=\"1333\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>CDC Director Robert Redfield testifying before the Senate on September 23, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/director-dr-robert-redfield-testifies-during-a-us-senate-news-photo/1228670522?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">ALEX EDELMAN/POOL/AFP via Getty</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Since joining the White House task force, Atlas has been widely criticized by scientists:</p><ul><li>In September, more than 100 of Atlas' former colleagues at <a href=\"https://www.mercurynews.com/2020/09/12/stanford-doctors-take-aim-at-former-colleague-scott-atlas-trumps-new-adviser-on-the-covid-19-pandemic/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"347c2f71d89b4484fdef3f26a50d09a3\">Stanford Medical School</a> signed a letter warning that many of his \"opinions and statements run counter to established science.\"</li><li>Bill Gates also suggested that Atlas was hired only because he \"agrees\" with what Gates called the White House's \"<a href=\"https://www.thesun.co.uk/news/12702442/bill-gates-trump-fauci-scott-atlas-crackpot-covid/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"ffe8cbd9804a404d46fb19ab76135d37\">crackpot COVID theories</a>.\"</li><li>Later that month, fellow task force member and top US infectious-disease expert Dr. Anthony Fauci <a href=\"https://edition.cnn.com/world/live-news/coronavirus-pandemic-09-28-20-intl/h_c19249ebeb35a18392b10e42b34827ac\">told CNN</a> he was concerned that Atlas was feeding information \"really taken either out of context or actually incorrect\" to the president.</li><li>Around the same time, CDC Director Robert Redfield was <a href=\"https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/politics-news/redfield-voices-alarm-over-influence-trump-s-new-coronavirus-task-n1241221\">overheard by a reporter criticizing</a> Atlas in a phone call, saying \"everything he says is false.\"</li><li>In October, former CDC Director William Foege <a href=\"https://eu.usatoday.com/story/news/investigations/2020/10/06/expert-cdcs-redfield-should-expose-trump-covid-failures-leave-post/5899724002/\">wrote</a> to Redfield saying the Trump administration had turned the CDC's reputation <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cdc-william-foege-letter-robert-redfield-resign-protest-white-house-2020-10\">\"from gold to tarnished brass.\"</a> Foege said Atlas' joining the task force was what prompted him to speak out.</li></ul><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f72fbf20ab50d00184ace92?format=jpeg\" alt=\"anthony fauci\" height=\"1334\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Dr. Anthony Fauci testifying before the Senate on September 23, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/director-of-the-national-institute-of-allergy-and-news-photo/1228670907?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">GRAEME JENNINGS/POOL/AFP via Getty</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>In response to Redfield and Fauci's criticism, Atlas told Business Insider in late September: \"All of my policy recommendations to the president are directly backed by the current science, and they are in line with what many of the world's top medical scientists advise ... Career government public health officials do not have a monopoly on knowledge.\"</p><p>In another<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/scott-atlas-hits-back-critics-questioning-science-fauci-redfield-2020-10\"> interview with Business Insider</a> in early October, Atlas accused his critics of being \"either politically motivated or are interested in maintaining their own stature in the public eye.\"</p><p>He added that he is working at the White House \"because the country's off the rails,\" not for any political reason.</p><h2>Pro-lockdown, pro-reopening</h2><p>Since the beginning of the US coronavirus outbreak, Atlas has spoken out against imposing lockdown measures, saying they were costing the lives of people too afraid to seek emergency medical treatment for other issues.</p><p>\"In the absence of immunization, society needs circulation of the virus, assuming high-risk people can be isolated,\" he wrote in an op-ed for <a href=\"https://thehill.com/opinion/healthcare/492514-reentry-after-the-panic-paying-the-health-price-of-extreme-isolation\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Hill</a> in April. \"It is very possible that whole-population isolation prevented natural herd immunity from developing.\"</p><p>The Washington Post <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/trump-coronavirus-scott-atlas-herd-immunity/2020/08/30/925e68fe-e93b-11ea-970a-64c73a1c2392_story.html?hpid=hp_hp-banner-low_virustrump-7am%3Ahomepage%2Fstory-ans\">reported</a> in August that Atlas had been pushing for the US to embrace herd immunity, though he has vehemently denied it.</p><p>Experts have <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fauci-herd-immunity-approach-not-resolving-pandemic-2020-9\">spoken out against herd immunity</a> — a scenario where enough people in a population become immune to a virus to stop it from spreading — warning that it would cost even more lives.</p><p>\"I have never advocated a herd-immunity strategy. That was a lie from the get-go,\" Atlas told Business Insider in early October, adding: \"But to deny herd immunity exists is to deny gravity. That is what I would call today's flat-earth movement.\"</p><p>Most recently, in mid-November, Atlas <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/scott-atlas-tweets-rise-up-against-michigan-coronavirus-restrictions-2020-11\">tweeted that the citizens of Michigan should \"rise up\"</a> against new coronavirus restrictions that had been rolled out to tackle a rise in cases in the state. After facing criticism for the tweet, he later clarified that he would \"NEVER .... endorse or incite violence.\"&#160;</p><p>Atlas was also <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/scott-atlas-appeared-on-russian-propaganda-outlet-and-slammed-lockdowns-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">forced to apologize</a> in early November after he gave an interview to Russian propaganda network RT about how lockdown policies were \"killing people.\" Atlas said he was \"unaware\" RT is a \"registered foreign agent\" and that he regretted the decision to speak with them.&#160;</p><p>In mid-October, Twitter <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tweet-removed-dr-scott-atlas-masks-dont-prevent-covid-19-2020-10\">removed a tweet by Atlas</a>, which said: \"Masks work? NO,\" alongside a link to an article that argued against the success of face coverings in stopping the spread of the coronavirus. Atlas later&#160;<a href=\"https://www.newsweek.com/twitter-removes-mask-tweet-white-house-adviser-1540081\">told Newsweek</a> that he has appealed the platform's decision.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f72fc3a74fe5b0018a8de11?format=jpeg\" alt=\"scott atlas\" height=\"1333\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Atlas addressing the media at the White House on September 28, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/dr-scott-atlas-advisor-to-president-donald-trump-delivers-news-photo/1277213737?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">Tasos Katopodis/Getty</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>'Any way I can help, I will do so'</h2><p>Since May, Atlas has regularly appeared on Fox News to speak on the US coronavirus crisis, and shared opinions often at odds with many public-health experts' warnings.</p><p>For example, Atlas had argued for schools to reopen for in-person classes and for the <a href=\"https://www.fox8tv.com/dr-scott-atlas-backs-calls-to-play-college-football-this-fall-we-have-to-become-rational-here/\">college football season to start</a> without any issues — ideas that some experts warned against, but which lined up with the president's own views.</p><p>In an interview with <a href=\"https://uk.news.yahoo.com/dr-scott-atlas-role-advising-002530721.html?guccounter=1&guce_referrer=aHR0cHM6Ly93d3cuZ29vZ2xlLmNvbS8&guce_referrer_sig=AQAAAKyiMz2TC2DFvPq2ACp7d9WOjNg7zx5LJQDCYC2VfR5skxdWtUgInEK_SPzp6OpIutZ--w1_oUlpeBMwBpMVmxtVK-m_W6O55yawJgpFiX2ISBRCvxtpLnq7J28gxDQf223Hv0-xuB2k3AX8Fjf1zNBtJkaOZ2UmrCHNBgohvKQnBgohvKQn\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Fox News</a> after his hiring, Atlas said of his new role: \"Any way I can help, I will do so.\"</p><p>When he hired Atlas in August, Trump called him a \"very famous man who's also very highly respected,\" according to a pool report.</p><p>\"He has many great ideas,\" Trump added. \"He thinks what we've done is really good, and now we'll take it to a new level.\"</p><p>But Trump's enthusiasm for Atlas has not saved him from a high-profile slight from the president, who forgot his name in an NBC News presidential town hall event in October.&#160;</p><p>Trump called Atlas \"Scott Adkins\" and \"Dr. Scott\" before calling him a \"great guy\" and \"one of the experts of the world,\" <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/trumps-den-of-dissent-inside-the-white-house-task-force-as-coronavirus-surges/2020/10/19/7ff8ee6a-0a6e-11eb-859b-f9c27abe638d_story.html\">according to The Washington Post's transcript</a>.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f37c718e89ebf001f044fd4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"teachers protest\" height=\"1900\" width=\"2533\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Teachers who oppose schools reopening during the COVID-19 pandemic in Tampa, Florida, on August 6, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Octavio Jones/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Atlas' rise at the White House coincided with the Trump administration's sidelining of Fauci, who has contradicted and corrected Trump's statements about the coronavirus throughout the pandemic.</p><p>Fauci has remained one of the most trusted sources for health information, while Trump has received unfavorable ratings for his coronavirus response.</p><div 22:27:42","updatedTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:42","title":"How to rediscover happiness in everyday life during the src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bbbd1e3e7670011716360?format=jpeg\" alt=\"businesswoman looking at phone in city walking\" height=\"1762\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Finding beauty in the mundane can help us approach life in a healthier, happier way.\n<p class=\"copyright\">mapodile/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Polina Marinova is the founder and author of&#160;<a href=\"https://theprofile.substack.com/\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"https://theprofile.substack.com/\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://theprofile.substack.com/&source=gmail&ust=1593205833501000&usg=AFQjCNE9bjciSqIGeHGkAeAFX8Y9-Rga7AAFX8Y9-Rga7A\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\">The Profile</a>, a newsletter that features longform profiles on successful people and companies.</li>\n<li>During the pandemic, she says it can feel easier than ever to get caught up in our pixelated appearances on Zoom meetings or compare ourselves to people on Instagram.</li>\n<li>If you want to survive in a world \"designed to depress us,\" Marinova believes taking the time to find small moments of joy in everyday life is the key to true happiness.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>When the pandemic first hit, we thought our lives would get more simple. We no longer had to worry about our outfits. We no longer had to figure out the logistics for getting to work, dropping the kids off, and making plans with friends. Our calendars were wiped clean.</p><p>But even though everything was stripped to its most bare-boned form, we still found things to worry about.</p><p>We started getting on Zoom calls, and suddenly, we began obsessing over our pixelated appearance. This has led to \"perceptual distortion,\" which occurs when we \"highlight a fault, then focus disproportionately on it until it becomes magnified\" in our perception. Our smartphones can further alter body image, due to the angles at which we hold them. As a result, the plastic surgery industry has&#160;<a href=\"https://www.bbc.com/worklife/article/20200909-why-plastic-surgery-demand-is-booming-amid-lockdown\">exploded in popularity</a>&#160;over recent months.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tips-help-small-business-owners-entrepreneurs-have-good-mental-health\">7 ways entrepreneurs and business owners can better manage their mental health and wellbeing</a></em></p><p>\"Celebrities have to look good in front of people,\"&#160;<a href=\"https://www.bbc.com/worklife/article/20200909-why-plastic-surgery-demand-is-booming-amid-lockdown\">said Gordon Lee</a>, a plastic and reconstructive surgeon. And now, for many who are living through the Zoom Boom, \"so do regular people\".</p><p>One of life's great ironies is that simplicity has become pretty complicated. Technology was supposed to make our lives easier — and it has, in many ways — except it hasn't made them&#160;<em>simpler</em>.</p><p>There's always a notification here, an email that needs responding there. Things compete for your attention at all hours in the night. In turn, this \"easy\" world has made us reactive, defensive, worried, and distracted.</p><p>As a result of the pandemic, we now&#160;<em>live</em>&#160;online. We've begun to over-identify with our virtual selves more so than with our un-filtered regular selves.</p><h2>Happiness has never felt more elusive. That's because we think happiness stems from success and appearance and money and&#160;<em>stuff</em>. That's not happiness; that's excess.</h2><p>I've written about&#160;<a href=\"https://theprofile.substack.com/p/the-profile-the-man-cleaning-up-facebook\">minimalism</a>&#160;before, and noted that the worst form of excess is to achieve everything you've ever dreamed of and realize that somehow you're&#160;<em>still</em>&#160;not happy and that something is&#160;<em>still</em>&#160;missing. And that, my friends, sucks.</p><p>There's this famous passage from Matt Haig's memoir \"<a href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25733573-reasons-to-stay-alive\">Reasons to Stay Alive\"</a>:</p><p>\"The world is increasingly designed to depress us. Happiness isn't very good for the economy. If we were happy with what we had, why would we need more?</p><p>\"How do you sell an anti-aging moisturizer? You make someone worry about aging. How do you get people to vote for a political party? You make them worry about immigration. How do you get them to buy insurance? By making them worry about everything. How do you get them to have plastic surgery? By highlighting their physical flaws. How do you get them to watch a TV show? By making them worry about missing out. How do you get them to buy a new smartphone? By making them feel like they are being left behind.</p><p>\"To be calm becomes a kind of revolutionary act. To be happy with your own non-upgraded existence. To be comfortable with our messy, human selves, would not be good for business.\"</p><p>So this leads me to my grandmother's neighbor Ivan. He lives in a small town near the Rila mountains in Bulgaria where it's not uncommon to see sheep, chickens, and cows just casually wandering around.</p><p>Ivan has animals, he does a ton of physical work every day, and he seems genuinely happy. His biggest worry the last time I saw him was how horrible airplanes are for the environment and how he sees them in the sky every day now.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc2c195037cbd0018612bdc?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Ivan Polina Marinova\" height=\"1092\" width=\"1456\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Polina Marinova&#39;s grandmother&#39;s neighbor Ivan.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Courtesy of Polina Marinova</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/former-chef-restaurateur-founded-snack-brand-split-overcame-addiction-2020-11\">A chef and restaurateur founded a successful snack brand after overcoming addiction. He shared how investing in his self-care made him a better leader and entrepreneur.</a></em></p><p>He couldn't care less about anti-aging moisturizer, plastic surgery, or smartphones. He may lead a simple life, according to our standards, but it's not in any way less busy or fulfilling.</p><p>It's not that Ivan doesn't have problems in his life, it's that he's learned how to find beauty in the mundane. For example, he loved this picture so much, he asked my grandmother to get it printed so he could frame it. He had never had a picture with his sheep before. It's a life of minimalism, but it's also a life of deliberately finding small, daily moments of joy.</p><p>So here's one thing we can all take away: Rather than obsessing over what we perceive as flaws, maybe for once we could appreciate the wrinkle or the gray hair that we see on our Zoom screens. It's a revolutionary act to notice those tiny moments of beauty so we can stop stuffing the pockets of beauty brands and plastic surgeons.</p><p>As Haig wrote, \"Wherever you are, at any moment, try and find something beautiful. A face, a line out of a poem, the clouds out of a window, some graffiti, a wind farm. Beauty cleans the mind.\"</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc60fc450e71a00115581cf?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mitch McConnell.\" height=\"2625\" width=\"5250\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Sen. Mitch McConnell.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Chip Somodevilla/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Senate Majority Leader Mitch McConnell said Monday there is \"no reason\" Congress can't quickly agree a new round of coronavirus stimulus.</li>\n<li>Democrats and Republicans have been at an impasse for months, with Republicans seeking a slimmer deal and Democrats looking for more.</li>\n<li>Time is short: Congress is meeting for a short session due to end by Christmas, and also has to avert a government shutdown.</li>\n<li>Among the issues to be thrashed out are whether to send another round of $1,200 direct payments to Americans.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Senate Majority Leader Mitch McConnell acknowledged the mounting pressure to deliver another round of economic stimulus, and said there is \"no reason\" that it couldn't be done by the end of 2020.</p><p>Democrats and Republicans have been in a deadlock over introducing new stimulus, with Democrats looking to pass a much bigger package than GOP lawmakers will approve.</p><p>The last coronavirus relief package was passed in spring, and expired in July. In the meantime, many American businesses and households continued to suffer the economic fallout of the COVID-19 pandemic.</p><p>McConnell said on the Senate floor on Monday that Congress had a number of things it \"should get done before the end of the year.\"</p><p>And he added: \"There is no reason – none – why we should not deliver another major pandemic relief package to help the American people through what seems poised to be the last chapters of this battle.\"</p><p>Lawmakers are only sitting for a few weeks, and also hope to address a looming government shutdown due to kick in on December 11, leaving little time for McConnell's ambition to come true.</p><p>As Business Insider's Tom Porter reported on Monday, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/congress-pressure-pass-covid-19-stimulus-brief-window-2020-11\">both President Donald Trump and President-elect Joe Biden have called on Congress</a> to come to an agreement.</p><p>Congressional leaders from both parties have continued to attack each other in recent days.</p><p>On Monday McConnell described the two leading Congressional Democrats, House Speaker Nancy Pelosi and Senate Minority Leader Chuck Schumer, as carrying out \"all-or-nothing obstruction.\"</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Leader McConnell  (@senatemajldr) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1333515616792272896?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">November 30, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>Pelosi and Schumer wrote to McConnell in November, arguing for more spending than the GOP has been willing to approve.</p><p>They said: \"It is essential that this bill have sufficient funding and delivers meaningful relief to the many Americans who are suffering,\" The New York Times <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/11/22/business/economy/biden-coronavirus-stimulus-recession.html?action=click&module=RelatedLinks&pgtype=Article=Article\">reported</a>.</p><p>Democrats <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-congress-big-focused-coronavirus-relief-bill-2020-11\">have proposed a $2.2 trillion relief plan</a> with a revival of the $600 weekly unemployment benefit from the CARES Act, a second round of $1,200 direct payments for Americans, aid for small businesses, and funding for state and local governments.</p><p>Republicans have proposed a smaller relief package, arguing that the economy is better than expected. In September, they <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stimulus-bill-democrats-block-skinny-gop-coronavirus-aid-unemployment-2020-10\">unveiled a $500 billion package</a> that included small-business relief and public-health funding.</p><p>Senate Republicans did not include another round of $1,200 checks in their latest relief bill in October, <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/11/23/economists-want-second-1200-stimulus-checks-where-the-relief-stands.html\">per CNBC</a>, though the parties had earlier <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/10/12/second-1200-stimulus-checks-have-been-discussed-for-5-months.html\">signaled an agreement</a> on sending more checks.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/11/22/business/economy/biden-coronavirus-stimulus-recession.html?action=click&module=RelatedLinks&pgtype=Article=Article\">CNN reported Monday</a> that the Congressional leaders are not negotiating with each other directly, but that their staffs are talking.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/obamas-former-top-economist-democrats-smaller-stimulus-package-now-2020-11\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"413ae06e71dfebaa04858eb5eb35c88d\">Many economists are urging</a> lawmakers to pass another relief package in order to minimize the economic blow of the pandemic</p><p><a the end of the year.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a essential for making smart decisions about the future.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Growing your business can feel especially difficult when juggling multiple duties at once, especially during the pandemic, so focusing on small, meaningful tasks can make a big difference.</li>\n<li>Whether it's creating a website, promoting your service on social media, or developing an email list, building a digital presence can drastically enhance your visibility online.</li>\n<li>Nurturing relationships with customers, suppliers, and employees to provide the best customer service possible can also offer a powerful boost to your business' bottom line.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Having your&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/business\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/business\">business</a>&#160;turn into a success is&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/hard-work\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/hard-work\">hard work</a>, and you need to adapt to the times while organizing things as you go. There are several actions you can do to help your business increase its revenue. Making sure each area of your company gets attention is crucial to ensure small things don't fall by the wayside.&#160;</p><p>As a business owner, you may feel as&#160;though you're juggling a hundred things at once. This is because you have to wear a lot of different hats when managing their company. They need to check possible ways of improving their daily operations.&#160;</p><h2>1. Build your website&#160;</h2><p>Having a user-friendly site that's up to date is a vital part of growing your company. A website design that's modern and functional will keep your enterprise moving forward. In today's competitive market, having a presence is not enough.</p><p>An optimized and well-designed site can help your business generate new leads and provide an increase in your overall conversion rate. Reward customers for visiting your online space through promotional offers and discount deals.&#160;</p><h2>2. Know your competition</h2><p>Knowing what your competitors are doing is a great way to improve how you're operating. You might be able to learn something from them. Strategies they've been using for years will be new to you and may offer a great payoff.&#160;</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/girls-night-in-newsletter-alisha-ramos-loyal-subscriber-audience-2020-11\">The founder of the Girls' Night In newsletter built her subscriber list to 170,000 people in less than 4 years. Here are her best tips for growing a loyal audience.</a></em></p><h2>3. Value creativity</h2><p>Standing out from your competitors is an essential step in growing any enterprise. Be open to any new ideas and remember that creative solutions can come from a lot of places. You can do innovative things like hosting events to promote new products you have.&#160;&#160;</p><h2>4. Provide great service</h2><p>Customer service is something that can either make or break a business. If a client feels heard and acknowledged, chances are they'll stay loyal. You need to make a point of going the extra mile, increasing the likelihood that clients will refer you. &#160;</p><h2>5. Understand your customer</h2><p>Your consumers are the core of your company. They're the lifeblood of any industry, and that's why you need to make sure you know what they want and need. Make use of&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/consumer\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/consumer\">consumer</a>&#160;feedback to improve how you deal with your client base.&#160;</p><h2>6. Get a grip on&#160;social media&#160;</h2><p>Promoting your business using social media platforms can increase your customer reach and allow you to gain information from them. Tracking what consumers are saying about your company online gives you an invaluable insight into their experience. It also provides you with a great place to advertise to potential clients.&#160;</p><h2>7. Develop&#160;an email list</h2><p>A quick and effective way to reach a vast amount of clients is through an email list. This requires you to have a funnel through which to generate leads. Ensure that your sales department understands the importance of sourcing these and turning them into active clients.&#160;</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/job-diary-fruit-instagram-influencer-17000-business-2020-11\">I'm a 29-year-old Instagram influencer who made $17,000 in one month. Here's how I turned my love of fruit into a lucrative business.</a></em></p><h2>8. Expand your network</h2><p>We all know the phrase, \"It's not<em>&#160;what&#160;</em>you know, but rather&#160;<em>who</em>&#160;you know.\" Networking is a great way to expand your professional relationships and gain insight into how others in the market are coping. It will also allow you to potentially meet investors that can improve the health of your enterprise.&#160;</p><h2>9. Amp up your exposure</h2><p>No one will work with you if they don't know your company exists, so increasing your visibility is crucial. Optimizing your SEO will increase the likelihood that you'll show up on one of the first pages of an internet search. If you're operating from a physical location, make sure it's visible on apps like Google Maps so consumers can find you.&#160;</p><h2>10. Nurture supplier relationships</h2><p>Your suppliers are an essential part of your enterprise. If you maintain a good relationship with them, they'll be more likely to help you out if problems arise in the future. Try to make sure the exchanges are mutually beneficial and don't be late with your payments.&#160;</p><h2>11. Focus on&#160;training your staff</h2><p>Having a competent team in place will help you delegate responsibilities and build your enterprise into a success. Improving your employee's sense of importance within the company will give them more&#160;incentive&#160;to work hard and do their best. Provide them with opportunities to get training and improve their knowledge base for a more rounded experience</p><h2>12. Know your finances</h2><p>Understanding the financial health of your company is essential to have a healthier bottom line. It's good to keep track of the business's debt so that you know what choices you can make for your company's future.&#160;&#160;</p><p>Keeping your enterprise going through tough times can be difficult, but it can be done if you're willing to put in the work. Your company can always stand to adapt to innovations in the market.&#160;</p><p>Ensure you have a website and are present on social media, create email lists to generate leads. Check out what your competition is doing, learn from them, but stand out.&#160; Nurture your relationships with your suppliers, employees, and clients. Putting in the extra time now will help you reap the rewards in the future.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a step down in 2021 as previously announced upon reaching the statutory term of 12 years,\" Switzerland's second-biggest bank said in a <a 12-year boardroom stint, first as vice-chairmen and since 2011 as chairman.</p><p>News of Osario's appointment came a day after a replacement was announced for the 56-year-old Portuguese native at Lloyds, with HSBC banker Charlie Nunn due to take over from him in 2021.</p><p>Horta-Osorio revived Lloyds in the aftermath of its 2008 government rescue during the financial crisis, with the bank returning to private ownership in 2017.</p><p>During his time at Lloyds, the Portuguese banker won plaudits for championing mental health issues at companies after he was signed off work for two Doug Ducey of Arizona in Phoenix on July 1.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ross D. Franklin/AP Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Arizona's Republican governor, Doug Ducey, has defended his state's election procedures after President Donald Trump singled him out for attack.</li>\n<li>Ducey certified Arizona's election result in President-elect Joe Biden's favor on Monday, enraging the president.</li>\n<li>Trump <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BylSchjpN_o\">phoned in</a> to Arizona's election hearings on Monday, alleging \"horrible fraud\" on Ducey's part, and then <a href=\"https://twitter.com/DeanBrowningPA/status/1333506309191315457\">took his anger to Twitter</a>.</li>\n<li>Ducey then <a href=\"https://twitter.com/dougducey/status/1333603735855976450\">tweeted a thread</a> outlining his pride in the state's election procedures and his commitment to the law.</li>\n<li>Trump has hit out several times at GOP figures he's deemed insufficiently loyal as he continues to challenge the election.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Arizona's Republican governor hit back at President Donald Trump after the president slammed him for confirming that President-elect Joe Biden had won the state.</p><p>Gov. Doug Ducey on Monday formally certified that Biden had won Arizona by 10,457 votes, awarding the Democrat 11 electoral votes, after a set of hearings challenging the results.</p><p>Trump criticized Ducey early by <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BylSchjpN_o\">calling in</a> to the hearing and, provoking boos from supporters, saying without evidence that Ducey had shown \"such corruption, such horrible fraud.\"</p><p>Then, soon after Ducey certified the state for Biden, Trump began a Twitter rampage against him, including retweeting a meme accusing Ducey of corruption.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;John D ●  (@RedWingGrips) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1333493671019249664?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">November 30, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>The president also shared a post that said Ducey had \"betrayed\" Arizona, adding: \"TRUE!\"</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Donald J. Trump  (@realDonaldTrump) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1333556458575818754?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">November 30, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>He also shared several other tweets about Ducey and the state's election system.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc12a4250e71a0011557ada?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Trump \" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>President Donald Trump.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/Patrick Semansky</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>On Tuesday morning, Ducey responded in a nine-tweet thread defending his state's election procedures.</p><p>The governor did not mention Trump but said he had talked about his state's election system \"in the Oval Office.\"</p><p>\"I've been pretty outspoken about Arizona's election system, and bragged about it quite a bit, including in the Oval Office. And for good reason,\" he began.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Doug Ducey  (@dougducey) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1333603891863191552?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">December 1, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>In the thread, Ducey said Arizona had \"some of the strongest election laws in the country\" and noted that every vote's signature was required to be verified by hand.</p><p>He described how the state had used bipartisan poll observers and prohibited measures that Democrats had pushed for in some states, such as third-party ballot collection and allowing mail-in ballots to be received after Election Day.</p><p>He went on to throw down a gauntlet for legal challenge, which now must be filed within five days of the certification.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"none\">&#8212;Doug Ducey  (@dougducey) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1333605109444460544?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">December 1, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>Trump has not hesitated to criticize fellow Republicans if he does not deem them loyal enough, with RINO — an acronym for \"Republican in name only\" — a favored insult.</p><ul><li>On November 20, Trump took a swipe at <a href=\"https://twitter.com/realDonaldTrump/status/1329769666546372613\">Sen. Mitt Romney of Utah</a> and called him a RINO after the senator said he did not vote for Trump and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mitt-romney-rips-trump-for-his-latest-attempt-subvert-election-2020-11\">criticized his election-fraud claims</a>.</li><li>On November 22, Trump also singled out <a href=\"https://twitter.com/realDonaldTrump/status/1330556513589620736\">Gov. Larry Hogan of Maryland</a> for criticism and deemed him a RINO on Twitter after he broke ranks to urge the president to concede in the election.</li><li>On November 26, the president also called Georgia Secretary of State Brad Raffensperger — who said he and his family had voted for Trump in 2020 — an \"<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-calls-raffensperger-enemy-of-people-over-baseless-election-claims-2020-11\">enemy of the people</a>\" after the state voted for Biden.</li><li>And on November 29, Trump told Fox Business that he <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/brian-kemp-trump-georgia-voting-machines-raffensperger-election-2020-11\">regretted supporting</a> Gov. Brian Kemp of Georgia, citing the state's use of Dominion Voting Systems machines — which have been the subject of conspiracy theories — during the election.</li></ul><div class=\"read-original\">Read 22:27:42","updatedTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:42","title":"Amazon says this year's holiday shopping period has been its biggest ever.
