This year's Cyber Monday is expected to be the biggest online shopping day in US history, according to Adobe Analytics.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The 2020 holiday season has been Amazon's biggest yet, the e-commerce giant said in a <a href=\"https://www.aboutamazon.com/news/retail/supporting-small-saving-big-and-shopping-early\">blog post Tuesday</a>.</p><p>Independent businesses on the platform are seeing \"record demand,\" it added. These businesses sold goods totaling $4.8 billion between Black Friday and Cyber Monday, Amazon said, 60% up on last year.</p><p>\"Through Cyber Monday, 2020 has been the largest holiday shopping season so far in our company's history,\" Amazon said.</p><p>Current best-sellers include the Echo Dot, Barack Obama's presidential memoir \"A Promised Land,\" and a health and ancestry DNA test by 23andMe.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jeff-bezos-amazon-culture-customer-obsession-build-empire-2020-11?r=gd-sub\">How Jeff Bezos' \"customer obsession\" transformed Amazon from an online bookseller into a $1.4 trillion retail giant that's burrowed into every corner of daily life</a></em></p><p>This record growth in online sales isn't just limited to Amazon.</p><p>Cyber Monday 2020 was <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cyber-monday-online-shopping-biggest-history-analysts-2020-11\">expected to be the biggest online shopping day in US history so far</a>, with digital sales reaching $12.7 billion, according to estimates from Adobe Analytics. This is a rise of more than a third compared to Cyber Monday 2019.</p><p>US consumers <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/black-friday-sees-record-online-as-us-shoppers-stay-home-2020-11\">spent a record $9 billion online on Black Friday</a>, Adobe Analytics said, which was an increase of around 22% from last year, as&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/black-friday-shopping-us-dropped-52-percent-says-sensormatic-solutions-2020-11\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"f42d93ac2aef8ec07b19c6b918d3f7be\">in-store shopping plummeted</a>.</p><p>Total US online sales over the holiday shopping season will reach around $189 billion, Adobe Analytics added. This represents two years of growth in just one season.</p><h2>Holiday shopping has started earlier than ever</h2><p>More customers than ever started their holiday shopping early, Amazon said.</p><p>As well as starting holiday shopping, people have also been listening to festive music earlier than usual. Global requests for holiday playlists and stations on Amazon Music via its home assistant Alexa have increased 90% compared to this time last year, Amazon said.</p><p>Customers have also been looking for self-care, cozy comfort, and&#160;nesting at home products as people continue to work from home. The most popular categories include beauty, home, fashion, sports, and pets, Amazon said.</p><p>Best-selling toys include the Lego Star Wars Mandalorian Battle Pack, Hot Wheels 20 Car Gift Pack, and L.O.L. Surprise! Present Surprise Doll, while Amazon fashion trends include colorful sports wear, tie-dye, and animal print.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a California on October 10, 2019. (Photo by Yichuan Cao/NurPhoto via Getty Images)\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2223\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>SpaceX CEO Elon Musk.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Yichuan Cao/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>SpaceX CEO Elon Musk said Sunday the next Starship test will happen \"no earlier than Wednesday.\"</li>\n<li>The spacecraft will fly 15 kilometres (50,000 feet) into the air. Previous prototypes have only made short hops of a few hundred metres.</li>\n<li>Musk said there was a lot that could go wrong, and gave the rocket a one-in-three chance of landing in one piece.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>This week, Elon Musk's space-exploration company SpaceX will take a big step forward in its quest to fly people to Mars.</p><p>Musk <a href=\"https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/1333123173815087111\">tweeted</a> on Sunday that SpaceX's enormous Starship spacecraft – which the company eventually wants to use to get humans to Mars – will undergo its first high altitude test as early as Wednesday.</p><p>This follows a successful test firing of the current prototype's engines on November 24.</p><p>On Sunday, a Twitter user highlighted an alert notice sent out to residents of Boca Chica village in southern Texas about SpaceX flight activities on Monday.</p><p>In response, Musk replied: \"Just a static fire tomorrow. Flight no earlier than Wednesday.\"</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Elon Musk  (@elonmusk) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1333123173815087111?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">November 29, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>According to Musk, in this week's test the rocket will fly 15 km (50,000 feet) into the air. Previous prototypes have made short hops a few hundred meters into the air.</p><p>This test flight will be a big step in testing whether the design can withstand the rigors of spaceflight.</p><p>Elon Musk said in a follow-up tweet on Wednesday that lots could go wrong in this first high-altitude test.</p><p>\"Lot of things need to go right,\" the billionaire <a href=\"https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/1331388984023461888\">said. </a></p><p>When asked on Twitter what he thought the odds were of Starship landing in one piece, he said it was one in three.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Elon Musk  (@elonmusk) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1331388984023461888?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">November 25, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>There are also more prototypes lined up to be tested should this one fail.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-starlink-satellite-dish-user-terminal-cost-stmelectronics-outsource-manufacturer-2020-11?r=ih-sub\">SpaceX may spend billions to outsource Starlink satellite-dish production, an industry insider says — and could lose $2,000 on each one it sells</a></em></p><p>SpaceX's Starship spacecraft is made up of two sections, the Super Heavy booster and the Starship rocket ship – which Musk claims will be able to carry 100 people to Mars at a time. The entire spacecraft stands at 120 metres (394 feet) tall.&#160;</p><p>There's no specific day confirmed for next week, and as <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/24/spacex-targeting-next-week-for-starships-first-high-altitude-test-flight/\">TechCrunch</a> notes, test dates are subject to change.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc0cace037cbd00186128a9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"SpaceX Starship.JPG\" height=\"3712\" width=\"4950\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A prototype of SpaceX&#39;s Starship spacecraft at the company&#39;s facility in Boca Chica, Texas (September 28, 2019).\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Callaghan O&#39;Hare</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>In October, Musk <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-starship-mars-elon-musk-rocket-2020-10?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">said</a> SpaceX has a \"fighting chance\" of sending an uncrewed Starship rocket to Mars in 2024, two years later than previously hoped.&#160;</p><p>Gwynne Shotwell, SpaceX's president and chief operating officer said October 23 the Starship rocket system could help solve the problem of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-starship-could-help-clean-up-space-junk-in-orbit-2020-11?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">space junk</a>.&#160;</p><p>\"It's quite possible that we could leverage Starship to go to some of these dead rocket bodies – other people's rockets, of course – basically, pick up some of this junk in outer space,\" she said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/epkA8sdGlr0\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 01 Dec 2020 09:44:35 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5fc0cd4f50e71a00115579a5?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"aefeca6ad7a3644963c78d15a166e295","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn4@2020_4/2020/12/01/14-28-12-582_628f151189cc4de4.webp","destWidth":1142,"destHeight":857,"sourceBytes":33922,"destBytes":33922,"author":"insider@insider.com (Isobel Asher Hamilton,Kate Duffy)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f496a007ffa48002894cf86?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn27@2020_5/2020/12/01/14-28-11-178_0f89c8169c3c0837.webp","https://i.insider.com/5fc0cace037cbd00186128a9?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn20@2020_5/2020/12/01/14-28-09-276_fec3a32f0f9f78b2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn19@2020_6/2020/12/01/14-28-10-417_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=epkA8sdGlr0:EQHAce3O4Eg:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn19@2020_6/2020/12/01/14-28-08-101_41c04fecaf4bb4c2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=epkA8sdGlr0:EQHAce3O4Eg:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn11@2020_3/2020/12/01/14-28-04-891_2d6ff36f295b8587.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn100@2020_6/2020/12/01/14-28-08-006_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=epkA8sdGlr0:EQHAce3O4Eg:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn64@2020_5/2020/12/01/14-28-07-168_03921ae640745a0c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/epkA8sdGlr0":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn96@2020_3/2020/12/01/14-28-09-463_667c8d50ffe96554.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1606832863084},{"createdTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:43","updatedTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:43","title":"Nike, Coca-Cola, and Apple reportedly lobbied to weaken a bill aimed at preventing them from manufacturing products in China using forced Uighur labor","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/apple-nike-coca-cola-lobbied-china-uyghur-forced-labor-bill-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc5ac9650e71a00115581ad?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hong Kong Uighur protest masks.JPG\" height=\"1998\" width=\"2664\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Hong Kong protesters rally in support of Xinjiang Uighurs&#39; human rights in Hong Kong, China, December 22, 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Lucy Nicholson</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Nike, Coca-Cola, and Apple were among the companies that lobbied to weaken a bill aimed at banning US firms from relying on Chinese forced labor, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/11/29/business/economy/nike-coca-cola-xinjiang-forced-labor-bill.html\">The New York Times</a>&#160;reported Sunday.</li>\n<li>HSBC, American Apparel, and several industry groups also lobbied on the bill, which would ban many goods imported from Xinjiang unless companies prove they weren't made with forced labor.</li>\n<li>The Uyghur Forced Labor Prevention Act, as it's called, passed the House in September by a 406-3 margin, and according to The New York Times, has the support needed to pass the Senate.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/china-kept-building-uighur-internment-camps-despite-release-claims-report-2020-9\">Various reports</a> have linked Nike, Coca-Cola, Apple, and other major US companies to suppliers in the region, where China has been accused of detaining and violating the rights of as many as one million Uighurs and other Muslim minorities.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Nike, Coca-Cola, and Apple all sought to weaken proposed legislation aimed at barring US companies from relying on the forced labor of Uighurs and other Muslim minorities in China's Xinjiang region, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/11/29/business/economy/nike-coca-cola-xinjiang-forced-labor-bill.html\">The New York Times</a>&#160;reported Sunday.</p><p>The Uyghur Forced Labor Prevention Act would ban US companies from importing a wide range of goods made in Xinjiang, where China has been accused of mass human rights violations unless companies can prove that the goods weren't made using forced labor.</p><p>The bill passed the House in September by a margin of 406 to 3, and aides told The&#160;Times that it has enough support to pass the Senate.</p><p>Other companies and trade groups, including HSBC, American Apparel, the National Retail Federation, and the US Chamber of Commerce also lobbied on the bill, according to lobbying disclosure forms.&#160;</p><p>None of the above organizations responded to a request for comment on this story.</p><p>Apple took issue with the claim that it tried to water down the bill in a statement to The Times.</p><p>Nike's global communications director, Greg Rossiter, told The Times that the company \"did not lobby against\" the bill but rather had \"constructive discussions\" with congressional staffers.</p><p>Coca-Cola told The Times in a statement that it \"strictly prohibits any type of forced labor in our supply chain.\"</p><p>The US Chamber of Commerce declined to comment to The Times. It instead referred it to a letter it and other groups wrote in November, saying they supported addressing forced labor.</p><p>Human rights groups, media reports, and other independent researchers have extensively documented China's <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/china-ijop-app-classifies-muslims-into-36-personality-types-xinjiang-uighurs-human-rights-watch-2019-5?r=ts-sub\">mass surveillance</a> and detainment of as many as one million Uighurs, Kazakhs, Kyrgyz, and other Muslim minority groups in internment camps, where reports allege they are subjected to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/life-inside-china-internment-camps-for-uighur-minority-in-xinjiang-bbc-report-2018-8?r=ts-sub\">torture</a>, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/uighur-activists-mass-rape-chinese-men-xinjiang-2019-12?r=ts-sub\">sexual abuse</a>, and forced labor for little or no pay.</p><p>In March, a report by the Australian Strategic Policy Institute (ASPI), which estimated that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/apple-forced-uighur-labor-iphone-factory-2020-3?r=ts-sub\">80,000 Uighurs have been forcibly relocated to factories across China</a>, found evidence of forced Uighur labor at four separate factories in Apple's supply chain as well as the supply chains of Nike, BMW, and Amazon.</p><p>Also in March, the Congressional-Executive Commission <a href=\"https://www.cecc.gov/sites/chinacommission.house.gov/files/documents/CECC%20Staff%20Report%20March%202020%20-%20Global%20Supply%20Chains%2C%20Forced%20Labor%2C%20and%20the%20Xinjiang%20Uyghur%20Autonomous%20Region.pdf\">said in a report</a> that Nike and Coca-Cola, as well as major brands such as Adidas, Campbell Soup, Costco, H&#38;M, Kraft Heinz, Patagonia, and Tommy Hilfiger, were suspected of relying on forced Chinese labor.</p><p>Nike claimed in a <a href=\"https://purpose.nike.com/statement-on-xinjiang\">March statement</a> that it \"does not source products\" from Xinjiang and that it \"confirmed with our contract suppliers that they are not using textiles or spun yarn from the region.\" Nike also told The&#160;Times that a factory in Qingdao that makes its shoes stopped using Uighur labor in 2019, though the ASPI report, citing Chinese state media, found that 800 Uighurs were still forced to work there as of November 2019.</p><p>Coca-Cola told The Times that a COFCO Tunhe plant in Xinjiang — that <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/western-companies-get-tangled-in-chinas-muslim-clampdown-11558017472\">The Wall Street Journal</a> reported last year was using forced labor — passed an independent audit in 2019 as well.</p><p>Amid growing bipartisan support for punishing China over the alleged human rights abuses, as well as holding companies accountable for exploiting it, US lawmakers introduced the Uyghur Forced Labor Prevention Act earlier this year. The bill could force companies — especially those with substantial supply chains in China, such as Nike, Coca-Cola, and Apple — to make major changes to how and where they manufacture their products, and is viewed as having more teeth than current laws.</p><p>In response, many companies have sought to weaken the disclosure and compliance requirements proposed in the bill.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2020/11/20/apple-uighur/\">The Washington Post</a> reported earlier this month that Apple had lobbied against the bill, and according to The&#160;Times, the tech giant pushed for longer deadlines to reach compliance, less disclosure to the general public, and putting more onus on the US government to assess whether Chinese entities are complicit in the oppression of Muslims.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2019-09-09/apple-foxconn-broke-a-chinese-labor-law-for-iphone-production\">Apple</a>, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/business/2005/apr/14/ethicalbusiness.money\">Nike</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.foodnavigator-asia.com/Article/2018/09/19/Coca-Cola-stands-firm-amid-criticism-of-human-rights-violations-in-South-East-Asia\">Coca-Cola</a> have over the years been accused by human rights groups of a variety of labor abuses and worker exploitation, particularly in China. They have also made <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/asia_pacific/nike-to-review-supply-chains-in-china-after-reports-uighurs-forced-to-make-shoes/2020/03/11/6137df9e-6380-11ea-912d-d98032ec8e25_story.html\">various pledges</a> and taken <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/11/09/apple-suspends-iphone-assembler-pegatron-over-labor-violations-in-china.html\">some steps</a> to address that criticism.</p><p>Monitoring that, however, has become difficult. Five major auditing groups hired by Western firms told <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/auditors-say-they-no-longer-will-inspect-labor-conditions-at-xinjiang-factories-11600697706\">The Wall Street Journal</a> in September that they are no longer carrying out supply chain inspections in China because restrictions imposed by government officials have made it too difficult to effectively and independently evaluate working conditions in the country.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/apple-nike-coca-cola-lobbied-china-uyghur-forced-labor-bill-2020-11'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 22:27:43","updatedTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:43","title":"Startups like Papa, which pairs elderly people with 'grandkids on demand' to help them with common tasks like grocery shopping, could be the future of healthcare. Here's an inside look at how it works.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/home-care-startups-like-papa-gig-economy-healthcare-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb6f44150e71a00115565c2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"senior 02\" height=\"3749\" width=\"4999\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Courtesy of Papa; Yuqing Liu/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The gig economy is coming for healthcare.</p><p>Startups like Papa, which provides \"grandkids on demand\" to seniors, hire mostly young part-time workers as outside contractors to help with chores, troubleshoot technology issues, or just sit and talk with seniors, many of whom have remained isolated during the coronavirus pandemic.</p><p>Big technology companies like Uber and Instacart popularized the gig&#160;model, but contract workers are nothing new in the world of home healthcare. With the advent of the gig economy, new home care startups have become empowered to introduce more flexibility and cost-savings into the industry by relying on a constantly rotating cast of always-on workers accessible via an app.&#160;</p><p>Business Insider spoke with nine Papa Pals, as Papa's fleet of on-demand grandkids are called, and Papa founder and CEO Andrew Parker to get a sense for what it's like to work as a gig worker in healthcare during a pandemic.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fbe84da50e71a00115575c6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Papa Pal\" height=\"902\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Florida-based Papa Pal Dejah Cason with Papa member Evelyn Perl.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Papa</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>Most joined this summer after hearing friends' positive experiences working with Papa, but others have worked for Papa on and off for years as they finished up school or managed their outside obligations. Business Insider reached out to Pals independently in addition to three conversations with Pals that were facilitated by Papa.<p><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/startups-like-papa-are-bringing-the-gig-economy-to-healthcare-2020-11?r=papa-teaser\">Here's the inside look of what it's like to work as a Papa Pal.</a></strong></p><p>The Pals shared a near-unanimous belief that they were doing good through their work providing companionship on-demand to elderly individuals. Many said they would continue calling or running errands once the pandemic subsides.</p><p>Others voiced some concerns with not being able to schedule shifts in advance, an issue Parker said an updated version of the app will address later this year.&#160;</p><p>There is also some concern among experts that the gig model won't be sustainable once the pandemic ends if health plans don't see enough impact to warrant continued support of this type of care.</p><p><strong>Subscribe to Business Insider to read the full story:</strong></p><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/startups-like-papa-are-bringing-the-gig-economy-to-healthcare-2020-11?r=papa-teaser\">Investors are betting $1.4 billion that gig workers can transform an essential but invisible part of healthcare. America</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\"><li>Chinese automaker Kandi's shares sank as much as 30% on Monday after Hindenburg Research accused the company of faking sales to raise $160 million from US investors.</li><li>Shares in the company continued to slide in pre-market trading on Tuesday after the short-seller reported more than half of Kandi's sales this year were Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li></ul><hr><p>Shares in <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/kndi-stock\">Kandi Technologies</a> tanked nearly 30% on Monday after a <a href=\"https://hindenburgresearch.com/kandi/\">scathing report</a> accused the Chinese automaker of faking sales and hyping its electric vehicle growth story.</p><p>The drop in the shares continued in pre-market trading on Tuesday. Kandi fell 9% to around $9.08 a share, as traders digested short-seller Hindenburg Research's claim that the company was \"using fake sales to undisclosed affiliates.\"</p><p>The Chinese manufacturer, which went public on the NASDAQ in 2008, raised $160 million from US investors in November alone.&#160;</p><p>Hindenburg said it had spoken to a dozen former employees and business partners to investigate Kandi's business, when it became apparent that the company's&#160;top customers were undisclosed entities. It found that almost 64% of Kandi's sales in the last twelve months were made to its own subsidiaries.&#160;</p><p>The company's largest customer, which accounted for about 55% of its sales in the last year, shared a phone number with a Kandi subsidiary, and an executive with the company, according to the Hindenburg report.</p><p>\"We visited the 'customer.' It is based in a tiny building right next to Kandi's factory with a sign indicating that it's a Kandi company,\" Hindenburg Research said. \"The same building housed another entity used by Kandi as part of a separate fake sales scheme to collect illegitimate subsidies from the Chinese government, for which it was fined and sanctioned.\"</p><p>Kandi told Business Insider it takes seriously any allegations of impropriety, and it would study Hindenburg's report. \"We intend to thoroughly research the accusations, investigate internally as needed, and offer a public response in the near future,\" a spokesperson said.</p><p><strong><em>Read More:</em></strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-covid-recovery-value-rotation-undervalued-rbc-2020-11\"><em>Buy these 10 stocks set to soar and smash Wall Street's expectations in the recovery from COVID-19, RBC says</em></a></p><p>Hindenburg, who has taken a short position in Kandi after extensive research, said it has photographic evidence to back up any claims of Kandi's \"customer\" inventory sitting in its own warehouse.</p><p>In addition to its concerns about Kandi's customer base, Hindenburg said the company had consistently booked revenue it can't collect and had a constantly-changing stream of executives at the top. It has had three auditors in the past five years, and four chief financial officers in the past four years.</p><p>The current auditor, Marcum, was recently banned by a regulatory authority from auditing Chinese companies. But instead of firing the auditor, Kandi reported an intention to renew its engagement.&#160;</p><p>Furthermore, the Chinese auto company has been \"launching\" in the US for over a decade. \"Its first US vehicles were imported illegally and seized by customs. A former distribution partner said every single car that eventually made it into the country broke,\" the report said.</p><p>In September, Hindenburg&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/nikola-short-seller-hindenburg-alleges-fraud-electric-trucks-trevor-milton-2020-9\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/nikola-short-seller-hindenburg-alleges-fraud-electric-trucks-trevor-milton-2020-9\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">accused</a> electric-truck maker Nikola of lying for years about its products and deals with other companies, days after the EV-maker announced a $2 billion deal with General Motors. Skipper/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A former Tesla employee will pay the electric-vehicle firm $400,000 for sharing trade secrets with the press, <a Tesla denied this claim.</p><p>He also filed a whistleblower <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/former-tesla-employee-files-tip-with-sec-2018-7\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"cf81a5a96ed0ba7f88ad4914964340c1\">tip with the US Securities and Exchange Commission</a> in which he claimed the automaker had overreported production of its Model 3 sedan by up to 44%. Tesla denied this claim, too.</p><p>Once Tripp was identified as the source of the information, Tesla fired him. Since then, Musk and Tripp have been locked in a bitter war of words — and lawsuits.</p><p>Tesla <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-sues-employee-elon-musk-said-committed-sabotage-2018-6\">filed a lawsuit</a> against Tripp in 2018 that accused him of hacking and of leaking \"confidential and trade secret information\" to third parties in a \"willful and malicious\" way \"with the deliberate intent to injure Tesla's business.\"</p><p>Musk also <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-employee-engaged-in-sabotage-against-the-company-report-2018-6\">accused him of \"sabotage.\"</a></p><p>Tripp maintained that he leaked the information because he was concerned about public safety and fired back with a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-martin-tripp-files-countersuit-2018-7\">countersuit of defamation</a>, which also accused Tesla of not living up to its environmental credentials.</p><p>Tripp also <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-whistleblower-martin-tripp-tweets-images-information-2018-8\">shared photos of the Gigafactory</a> on social media, which he argued supported his allegations about the safety and quality of Tesla's parts. The countersuit was thrown out by a judge, who said Tesla's behavior didn't show \"actual malice.\"</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/electric-car-race-over-tesla-won-musk-knows-doesnt-matter-2020-8?r=gd-sub\">Winning the electric-car race is just the beginning of Elon Musk's plan for Tesla</a></em></p><p>In a heated email exchange, Tripp accused Musk of telling lies to the public and investors, while <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-whistleblower-martin-tripp-elon-musk-waging-war-on-him-over-leaks-2018-6\">Musk called Tripp a \"horrible human being.\"</a></p><p>In December 2018, it was revealed that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-sues-ex-employee-martin-tripp-for-167-million-legal-filings-2018-12\">Tesla was suing Tripp for more than $167 million</a>, according to a legal filing from Tripp's defense team. His lawyers called the figure \"absurd.\"</p><p>This has since been reduced to $400,000, Bloomberg reported Tuesday.</p><p>The proposed settlement, which Tripp has agreed to, also included him admitting to violating trade-secret laws and confidentiality agreements, alongside a payment of $25,000 for continuing to share information about Tesla after being ordered to stop by a judge.</p><div 22:27:43","updatedTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:43","title":"Tony Hsieh, the late former CEO of Zappos, wrote the definitive playbook on corporate culture. Here are 4 lessons from his bestseller 'Delivering Happiness.'","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/tony-hsieh-lessons-summarized-delivering-happiness-2020-12","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc4e21e037cbd0018612cf8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tony Hsieh\" height=\"2592\" width=\"3888\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tony Hsieh was the former CEO of the e-commerce giant Zappos.com\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas SAMSON/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Tony Hsieh, the former leader of online retail giant Zappos, died suddenly on November 27.</li>\n<li>He is credited with influencing how businesses approach company culture and customer service, pioneering a philosophy of happiness above profits.</li>\n<li>That philosophy is laid out in his 2010 best-seller \"Delivering Happiness: A Path to Profits, Passion, and Purpose.\"</li>\n<li>The book remains highly influential a decade on. Scroll on to read four key lessons from Hsieh's work.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Tributes continue to pour in for Tony Hsieh, the entrepreneur famed for building online shoe and clothing giant Zappos.</p><p>Hsieh <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tony-hsieh-ex-ceo-zappos-died-aged-46-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">died on November 27</a>&#160; due to injuries he sustained from a house fire in Connecticut. He was 46 years old.</p><p>Tributes came from those who had not only met Hsieh but had read his highly influential first book \"<a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Delivering-Happiness-Profits-Passion-Purpose/dp/0446576220\">Delivering Happiness</a>.\"</p><p>The entrepreneur was widely credited for raising the bar for customer service in online retail, laying out his philosophy around happiness in the 2010 book. Hsieh and his cofounder Alfred Lin famously maintained a focus on Zappos' culture after its sale to Amazon in 2009.</p><p>The book was number one on the New Your Times Best Seller List the year of its release and it remains Amazon's number one bestseller in the law for small businesses section and number four in the site's entrepreneurship category.</p><p>Hsieh's lessons evidently still hold true a decade on. Here are four key lessons from the book:</p><h2>1. Find your one true passion and don't follow the money</h2><p>It's important to figure out the one thing you're passionate about, Hsieh wrote. If you have that in mind and know what your ultimate goal is, subsequent decisions will become easier to make.&#160;</p><p>\"You want to figure out the right balance of profits, passion, and purpose in business and in life,\" Hsieh wrote.</p><p>During his first couple of years at Zappos, Hsieh and his cofounder Alfred Lin struggled to make a profit and had only a couple of months' worth of cash.</p><p>Coming from their successful prior business, LinkExchange, they thought it would have been easy to raise new funds until it wasn't. They halted thinking solely about profit, were clear with their staff about the economic situation, cut jobs and salaries, and worked with the remaining of the team to find solutions to make the business profitable.</p><p>The remaining team stepped up and worked harder than before. The layoffs didn't hurt the company's productivity due to the staff's effort but also because they were passionate about the company, and believed in its future and potential.</p><p>\"It was a big lesson in the power of instilling passion throughout the entire company and working as a unified team. Everyone was making sacrifices,\" Hsieh wrote.</p><p>Hsieh wanted to transform Zappos from a good to a great company: \"Great companies have a greater purpose and bigger vision beyond just making money or being number one in a market,\" wrote Hsieh, citing the book \"Good to Great\" by Jim Collins. \"A lot of companies fall into the trap of just focusing on making money, and then they never become a great company.\"</p><h2>2. Hire the right people, have the right company culture, and the rest will develop</h2><p>Treat people well and only hire people you would hang out with outside of working hours. \"Many of the best ideas came about while having drinks at a local bar,\" said Hsieh. Those are the people who will make you want to go to work and feel part of a bigger family — the ''friends of Zappos\" in Hsieh's case — and therefore do whatever needed to make a company successful.</p><p>You also need to actively foster culture. \"You want to create a stronger company culture, which will make your employees and coworkers happier and create more employee engagement, leading to higher productivity,\" Hsieh wrote.</p><p>Culture was famously a major priority for Hsieh, who saw this as key to the success of the business. He asked all his staff to write down what the business meant to them, and made a book out of their thoughts — none being censored. Every year a new edition would be produced, with new sentences added and changed. Hsieh would give out that new version of the Zappos Culture Book to prospective employees, vendors, and even customers.&#160;&#160;</p><h2><strong>3. Surprise your customers and show them how much you care</strong></h2><h3><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc25c47037cbd0018612b96?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tony Hsieh\" height=\"683\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>&#34;You want to figure out the right balance of profits, passion, and purpose in business and in life,&#34; Hsieh wrote.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/january-8-las-vegas-nevada-tony-hsieh-ceo-of-zappos-speaks-news-photo/539692878?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">Chris Farina/Corbis via Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></h3><p>In 2003, the dot-com crash was still hammering Zappos' profit.</p><p>Hsieh decided to make customer service the focus of the business. He wrote that at the time it felt like the only choice for its survival but realized later on it was actually \"a blessing in disguise.\"</p><p>Good customer service builds a brand and drives word of mouth, he said.</p><p>\"Our philosophy has been to take most of the money we would have spent on paid advertising and invest it into customer service and the customer experience instead, letting our customers do the marketing for us through word of mouth,\" Hsieh wrote.</p><p>That involved measuring whether Zappos employees went \"above and beyond\" for customers, rather than measuring them on call volumes.</p><p>Another way was to continually \"wow\" customers — for example giving loyal customers overnight shipping even when they only promised the standard option.&#160;</p><h2>4. Make learning a priority for yourself and staff</h2><p>Hsieh called himself an \"avid book reader\" and made a compulsory book list for his staff. Zappos' office had a library with thousands of books and offered courses on the most important titles.</p><p>Continual growth should always be any business's priority, the entrepreneur wrote. And any workplace should appreciate employees spending time and effort into their personal and professional development, allowing them to take up challenges as soon as they are ready.&#160;</p><div 22:27:43","updatedTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:43","title":"Trump has raised at least $150 million to cover his bogus election challenges — but most of that money will go to financing Trump's future","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-campaign-election-challenge-fundraised-150m-most-money-future-plans-2020-12","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc61951037cbd001861307b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"donald trump\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>President Donald Trump at the East Room of the White House in the early hours of November 4, 2020, the day after Election Day.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/president-donald-trump-pumps-his-fist-after-speaking-during-news-photo/1229449739?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">Mandel Ngan/AFP via Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>In the month since Election Day, President Donald Trump's campaign has ratcheted up fundraising, raising more than $150 million, <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/trump-raises-more-than-150-million-appealing-to-false-election-claims/2020/11/30/82e922e6-3347-11eb-afe6-e4dbee9689f8_story.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Washington Post</a> reported on Monday.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/11/30/us/politics/trump-campaign-donations.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The New York Times</a> published a similar report on Monday, but put the number at $170 million.&#160;</li>\n<li>To put that into context, the amount raised since Election Day is about double the amount that one of Trump's main PACs raised during September, its best month.</li>\n<li>The Trump campaign sent hundreds of emails in November, asking supporters to donate as the president fights the results of the 2020 election, The Post reported.</li>\n<li>But the fine print shows that only a fraction of small-dollar donations go to the Trump campaign's legal fund, with most of the money going into a new account designated to seed his political future instead.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>President Donald Trump's campaign has raised at least $150 million after Election Day after sending out hundreds of emails asking for support as Trump continues his hopeless mission to contest President-elect Joe Biden's win, according to Monday reports from <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/trump-raises-more-than-150-million-appealing-to-false-election-claims/2020/11/30/82e922e6-3347-11eb-afe6-e4dbee9689f8_story.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Washington Post</a> and <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/11/30/us/politics/trump-campaign-donations.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The New York Times</a>.</p><p>In reality, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/donations-trump-leadership-pac-pay-family-finance-2024-presidential-bid-2020-11\" rel=\"noopener\">only a small fraction of small-dollar donations is being used for Trump's legal challenges</a>, with the vast majority instead being put into an account which the president can use to fund his post-White House political career.&#160;</p><p>The Post and Times reports differ slightly on the total raised by the Trump campaign since Election Day. The Post said that more than $150 million was raised in that time, citing multiple sources, while a source who spoke to The Times put that number at $170 million.&#160;</p><p>Regardless of the exact total, it's a significant amount for the campaign. For comparison, the Trump Make America Great Again Committee, one of Trump's main political action committees, raised $125 million in all of the second quarter of 2020, and raised $81 million during September, its best fundraising month, according to The Post.</p><p>Business Insider has contacted the Trump campaign for comment.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fbed0fc037cbd0018612701?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Joe Biden\" height=\"1328\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Joe Biden (pictured) has won the 2020 presidential election, but Trump has continued to contest the election results in several states.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Joshua Roberts/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>Hundreds of emails&#160;</h2><p>At a time when most losing campaigns start winding down, Trump's campaign took the unusual step and increased its calls for donations, The Post and The Times reported.</p><p>The campaign sent out hundreds of emails to donors in November, The Post reported.</p><p>The focus of the emails since Election Day has been on riling up supporters about Trump's unfounded claims of widespread voter fraud, giving supporters the impression that they're directly helping the campaign contest the election results in the courts with their donations.&#160;</p><p>According to The Post, one of these recent emails was a message to donors from Vice President Mike Pence, which read: \"Our democracy and freedom is at risk like never before, which is why I'm reaching out to you now with an URGENT request. President Trump and I need our STRONGEST supporters, like YOU, to join the Election Defense Task Force. This group will be responsible for DEFENDING the Election from voter fraud, and we really need you to step up to the front lines of this battle.\"</p><h2>Where the money is actually going</h2><p>The fine print on the donation page tells another story, though.</p><p>According to The Times, the email fine print says that nearly all small-dollar donations are split between the Save America PAC, new leadership PAC to fund the president's post-White House political future, and the Republican National Committee.</p><p>The emails added that donors have to spend&#160;$5,000 in order for part of their money to start going to Trump's legal fund. Until they hit that number, 75% goes to the new PAC and 25% goes to the RNC, according to The Times.&#160;</p><p>\"Small donors who give to Trump thinking they are financing an 'official election defense fund' are in fact helping pay down the Trump campaign's debt or funding his post-presidential political operation,\" Brendan Fischer, director of federal reform at the Campaign Legal Center — a nonpartisan nonprofit that works to reduce the influence of money in politics — told The Post.</p><p>\"The average donor who gives in response to Trump's appeal for funds to 'stop the fraud' likely doesn't realize that their money is actually retiring Trump's debt or funding his leadership PAC,\" he added.</p><p>The Times also noted that the Trump campaign is automatically signing donors up for repeated weekly contributions. Donors have to un-tick a box to opt out of the scheme, which some critics have called misleading, according to The Times.&#160;</p><p>As <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/donations-trump-leadership-pac-pay-family-finance-2024-presidential-bid-2020-11\">Business Insider</a> previously reported, a leadership PAC like the Save America PAC is typically created by current and former politicians, and can be used to fund travel and events.</p><p>The Post report pointed out that the money from this kind of PAC could even be used to pay for events at Trump's own properties. Leadership PACs are \"loosely regulated\" and do not face the same restrictions as candidate committees do, the newspaper reported.</p><ul class=\"read-more-links\"><li>Read more:</li><li><a 22:27:43","updatedTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:43","title":"Companies whose boards are entirely white men could be delisted from Nasdaq's US stock exchange under new proposals","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/nasdaq-companies-with-all-white-male-boards-face-delisting-2020-12","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc63be050e71a001155820e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Adena Friedman, Nasdaq\" height=\"1200\" width=\"1600\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Adena Friedman, Nasdaq CEO.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Nasdaq</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Nasdaq has said that companies listed on its main US stock exchange should have two \"diverse directors\" on the board.</li>\n<li>If they don't, they could be delisted, it said, as first reported by The New York Times DealBook.&#160;</li>\n<li>Under a proposal to be reviewed by the Securities and Exchange Commission, companies must have at least one woman director and one director who self-identifies as an underrepresented minority or LGBTQ+.</li>\n<li>Currently, three in four companies listed on Nasdaq's stock exchange don't meet these requirements.</li>\n<li>Companies that do not meet the requirements will not be delisted if they publicly explain themselves, Nasdaq said.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Companies listed on Nasdaq's US stock exchange will have to have at least one woman and another \"diverse\" director on their board under new proposals.</p><p>If companies don't meet the diversity requirements, they could be delisted.</p><p>The 3,249 companies listed on Nasdaq's main US stock exchange will have to have at least one female director and one director who self-identifies as an under-represented minority or LGBTQ+, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/12/01/business/dealbook/nasdaq-diversity-boards.html\">The New York Times DealBook</a> first reported Tuesday.</p><p>If they don't, they will have to publicly explain why they have not met the requirement, or face being delisted, Nasdaq said in a <a href=\"https://www.nasdaq.com/press-release/nasdaq-to-advance-diversity-through-new-proposed-listing-requirements-2020-12-01?utm_source=Nasdaq_TWITTER_4264244680&utm_medium=CorpGov+%28New%29__29__\">press release</a>.</p><p>Currently, three in four companies listed on Nasdaq don't meet these diversity requirements.</p><p>\"An 'underrepresented minority' is an individual who self-identifies in one or more of the following groups: Black or African American, Hispanic or Latinx, Asian, Native American or Alaska Native, Native Hawaiian or Pacific Islander, or two or more races or ethnicities,\" Nasdaq said.</p><p>\"It's not like we're saying this is an optimal composition of a board, but it's a minimum level of diversity that we think every board should have,\" Nasdaq CEO Adena Friedman told DealBook.</p><p>Nasdaq will ask the Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) for permission for the change on Tuesday. It will likely be weeks before the SEC reaches a verdict.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/companies-tying-executive-bonuses-meeting-diversity-esg-goals-2020-11?r=gd-sub\">Here's the plan Verizon uses to tie executives' pay to diversity and inclusion goals — and how other companies like Starbucks and Uber are following suit</a></em></p><p>Under Nasdaq's proposals, companies are expected to have at least one of the two \"diverse directors\" within two years, while the biggest companies will need one of each type of director within four years.</p><p>The companies will also have to&#160;report data on their board's diversity within a year of SEC approval.</p><p>Benefits of a diverse board range from higher-quality financial disclosures to fewer audit problems, Friedman said.</p><p>It follows large companies pushing for greater boardroom diversity.&#160;</p><p>Since July, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/goldman-sachs-wont-help-companies-ipo-without-diverse-boards-member-2020-1-1028841276\">Goldman Sachs has stopped doing IPOs for companies without at least one \"diverse\" board member</a>, with a focus on women.</p><p>\"We might miss some business,\" Goldman Sachs CEO David Solomon told CNBC in January after announcing the change. \"But in the long run, this I think is the best advice for companies that want to drive premium returns for their shareholders.\"</p><p>BlackRock is also trying to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/larry-fink-blackrock-diversity-black-women-senior-leadership-2020-9\">build a pipeline of female and Black leaders</a>.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the Joni Ernst, and Susan Collins.</li>\n<li>The Senate is likely going to be controlled by the Republican Party under the Biden administration, and Tanden may need GOP senators' votes to assume the OMB role.</li>\n<li>Her appointment has been controversial and former colleagues have <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/bidens-omb-pick-condemned-by-bernie-sanders-aligned-progressives-2020-11\">criticized her management style.</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Neera Tanden, President-elect Joe Biden's nominee for budget chief, has deleted hundreds of tweets in recent days, many of which were critical of Republican senators who will likely be voting on her appointment, <a href=\"https://www.thedailybeast.com/neera-tanden-mean-tweeted-gop-lawmakersuntil-she-needed-their-votes?ref=home?ref=home\">The Daily Beast reported.</a></p><p>Internet archives show that as of November 1, 2020, Tanden had posted 88,639 tweets, but as of Monday evening that number has dropped to 87,588.</p><p>A number of those tweets criticized senators like Mitch McConnell, Joni Ernst, and Susan Collins, who will vote on Biden's nomination for her to head the Office of Management and Budget next year.</p><p>A June 14, 2019, <a href=\"https://web.archive.org/web/20200218100156/https://twitter.com/neeratanden/status/1139526680211599361\">tweet deleted by Tanden</a> read: \"Can people on here please focus their ire on McConnell and the GOP senators who are Up This Cycle who enable him: Cory Gardner, Collins, Ernst, Cornyn, Perdue, Tillis And many more.\"</p><p>The Senate was controlled by the Republican Party during President Donald Trump's administration, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/2020-senate-election-results\">is likely to remain that way during the Biden presidency.</a></p><p>Another of Tanden's tweets, deleted some time since November 1, called Senate majority leader McConnell \"Moscow Mitch,\" a nickname he is <a href=\"https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/americas/us-politics/mitch-mcconnell-moscow-republican-senate-leader-2020-election-a9091276.html\">said to hate</a>, The Daily Beast reported.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc618a7037cbd0018613079?format=jpeg\" alt=\"AP mitch mcconnell\" height=\"1082\" width=\"2164\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Senate Majority Leader Mitch McConnell at the Capitol on October 26, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Manuel Balce Ceneta/AP Photo</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Business Insider has contacted Tanden for comment.</p><h2>Democrats, Republicans unhappy with Tanden's appointment</h2><p>A number of Republican figures have said publicly that Tanden is unlikely to be accepted by the Senate.</p><p>Drew Brandewie, a spokesperson for GOP Sen. John Cornyn, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/DBrandewie/status/1333205134004858889?s=20\">tweeted</a> on Monday that&#160;Tanden \"stands zero chance of being confirmed.\"</p><p>Cornyn also told reporters on Monday that Tanden may be Biden's \"worst nominee so far,\" <a href=\"https://twitter.com/JakeSherman/status/1333523740966195204\">according to Politico reporter Jake Sherman</a>.</p><p>Tanden's nomination has also not gone down well among former colleagues and some Democratic Party circles, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-neera-tanden-omb-cap-sexual-harassment-punched-reporter-2020-11\">with many criticizing her leadership style.</a></p><p>Tanden was described by Center for American Progress colleagues as \"impossible to trust\" after <a href=\"https://www.buzzfeednews.com/article/sarahmimms/inside-a-divisive-fight-over-how-a-top-progressive-think\">BuzzFeed News reported</a> that she had identified of a victim of sexual harassment in a company meeting.</p><p>A former senior Center for American Progress employee also <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/bidens-omb-pick-condemned-by-bernie-sanders-aligned-progressives-2020-11\">told Business Insider</a> that Tanden used the company as \"an engine for her ambition\" at her colleagues' expense.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc618c4037cbd001861307a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tanden speaks on the third day of the Democratic National Convention in Philadelphia\" height=\"1449\" width=\"2900\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tanden speaking on the third day of the 2020 Democratic National Convention in Philadelphia.\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Mike Segar</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Ali Gharib, a journalist who worked under Tanden on ThinkProgress, a now-shuttered news site connected to the Center for American Progress, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-neera-tanden-omb-cap-sexual-harassment-punched-reporter-2020-11\">tweeted on Monday</a> that she lacked \"leadership and moral courage.\"</p><p>Briana Gray, who worked as a press secretary on the Bernie Sanders campaign, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/briebriejoy/status/1333268563872899073?s=20\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"ed59f28aa8f85e1f6ac5fbd7fa316c2f\">also tweeted</a>&#160;that \"everything toxic about the corporate Democratic Party is embodied in Neera Tanden.\"&#160;</p><p>Tanden garnered unwanted newspaper headlines in 2008 when she was accused of punching a top editor at ThinkProgress after he asked her then-boss Hillary Clinton about the war in Iraq, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/04/15/us/politics/tanden-sanders-.html\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"e385712d2c809edbff573635aae0833c\">according to The New York Times.</a></p><p>Tanden later said it was a push, not a punch.</p><p>As Business Insider's Eliza Relman <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/bidens-omb-pick-condemned-by-bernie-sanders-aligned-progressives-2020-11\">previously reported</a>, Tanden is a longtime advisor to Clinton, and played a key role in her 2008 and 2016 presidential campaigns.</p><p>She also helped engineer the Affordable Care Act during former President Barack Obama's administration.&#160;</p><p>If Tanden is voted in as budget chief, she will be the first woman of color to hold the office. The agency is tasked with drafting and enacting out the US government's annual spending plan, and its leader has a seat in the <a href=\"https://www.whitehouse.gov/the-trump-administration/the-cabinet/\">presidential cabinet</a>.</p><p>Despite the criticism, a Biden transition official <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/bidens-omb-pick-condemned-by-bernie-sanders-aligned-progressives-2020-11\">told Business Insider</a> that Tandem is the right choice for the role.</p><p>\"The fact that Neera not only has the policy experience and expertise but also has the background to relate to all of those needs makes her an incredibly compelling choice to lead the office,\" the official said.</p><ul class=\"read-more-links\"><li>Read more:</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/joe-biden-senate-confirmation-fight-neera-tanden-economic-pick-2020-11\" distribution of its vaccine from regulators both in the United States and overseas.&#160;</p><p>Adding to the upbeat mood across the markets, official Chinese data showed factory activity in the world's second largest economy grew at its fastest pace since November 2010 last month, marking its seventh straight month of expansion and leaving behind the coronavirus-induced recession earlier this year.</p><p>Futures on the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/futures/s&p-500-futuresures\">S&#38;P 500</a>, the <a 1.0%, pointing to a strong start to trade after the opening bell.&#160;</p><p>In Europe, the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/ftse_100\">FTSE 100</a> rallied sharply, rising 1.5%. The index gained just over 12% last month, marking its strongest one-month increase in 29 years.&#160;</p><p>The <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/dax\">DAX</a> rose 1%, while the broader <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/stoxx_europe_600\">Stoxx 600</a> gained 0.7%, extending last month's record-breaking 14% rally. In Asia, the major indices posted strong gains overnight. Seoul's <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/kospi\">KOSPI</a> rose almost 2%, while the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/shanghai_composite\">Shanghai Composite</a> gained 1.8% and Tokyo's <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/nikkei_225\">Nikkei</a> closed 1.3% higher.&#160;</p><p>\"After a phenomenal November run-up European markets are broadly resuming gains at the start of December, a traditionally strong month for equities,\" CityIndex analyst Fiona Cincotta said in a note. \"Vaccine optimism, impressive Chinese factory data and the prospect of continuing fiscal and monetary stimulus is keeping the mood upbeat.\"</p><p><strong><em>Read More:</em></strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-covid-recovery-value-rotation-undervalued-rbc-2020-11\"><em>Buy these 10 stocks set to soar and smash Wall Street's expectations in the recovery from COVID-19, RBC says</em></a></p><p>A number of European countries have started to see the daily rise in cases and deaths from COVID-19 slow somewhat, after weeks of partial, or even total lockdowns. With the worst of the winter season yet to come and an effective vaccine some weeks, or even months, away, there is a degree of caution hanging over the financial markets.</p><p>Oil meanwhile eased after a group of the world's largest exporters delayed a key meeting to discuss their supply plans for 2021, over a lack of consensus on what any deal might look like.&#160;</p><p>The Organization of the Petroleum Exporting Countries, together with partners including Russia, Mexico and Oman, is holding a virtual meeting this week to hash out its supply plans for next year. Its existing agreement to curtail daily output by 7.7 million barrels a day expires at the end of December.&#160;</p><p>Since the group agreed in the spring to restrict output and protect the oil market from a damaging decline, the price of crude has risen by around 80% and, while a second wave of COVID-19 is threatening demand in the short-term, the rollout of a vaccine means movement is less likely to be restricted. An extension of the output cuts in their current form is now in question.</p><p>\"We still believe that the group will probably find some face-saving compromise, with a short extension being the most likely outcome followed by a phased production return,\" RBC commodities strategist Helima Croft said in a note.</p><p>\"Nonetheless this latest fracas does not bode well for collective cohesion in 2021 as vaccine optimism abounds and producers anticipate a strong recovery,\" she said.</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/oil-price\">Brent crude futures</a>, which are most sensitive to OPEC production, edged up 0.1% on the day to around $47.91 a barrel, having touched an earlier session low of $47.39, while <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/oil-price?type=wti\">US crude futures</a> were roughly unchanged around $45.35 a barrel, but off an intraday low of $44.83.&#160;</p><p><strong><em>Read More: </em></strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/goldman-sachs-esg-trends-markets-climate-investing-stock-sustainability-social-2020-11\"><em>A top equity portfolio strategist at Goldman Sachs shares his four essential ESG trends that you need to be thinking about</em></a></p><p>The <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/us-dollar-index\">dollar index</a> fell 0.3%, as investors pushed capital into more risk-exposed assets, such as emerging-market currencies, commodities and the crypto market.&#160; The dollar is trading around its lowest since mid-2018 against a basket of major currencies, reflecting the improvement in risk appetite that has accelerated in pace in the past few weeks.</p><p>Cryptocurrencies rallied for a second day, pushing the price of <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/btc-usd\">Bitcoin</a> up by 6% to around $19,585. Bitcoin hit a record $19,749.26 on the Binance exchange on Monday.&#160;Ripple's <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/xrp-usd\">XRP</a> rose nearly 9% to around $0.6675, having risen by almost 180% in November's massive crypto rally. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/eth-usd\">Ethereum</a>, meanwhile, gained 6.4% to trade around $612.92, nudging at its highest in two and a half years.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 22:27:43","updatedTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:43","title":"Elon Musk wanted to name his tequila 'Teslaquila,' but Mexico wouldn't let him","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-tesla-tequila-teslaquila-name-blocked-mexico-crt-2020-12","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa58ab81df1d5001821952d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"tesla tequila hero\" height=\"702\" width=\"937\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tesla Tequila launched in November.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tesla</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>In November, Elon Musk's Tesla brought out a novelty tequila called \"Tesla Tequila.\"</li>\n<li>Originally, Tesla filed to call the product \"Teslaquila,\" but it was blocked by Mexico's Tequila Regulatory Council.</li>\n<li>Essentially, if Tesla wanted to call its drink tequila, it had to use the word tequila without changing it so as to avoid diluting the brand.</li>\n<li>Tesla tried to argue that the brand name was just \"Tesla\" with \"quila\" attached, but the Mexican Institute of Industrial Property refused to let it register the name.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Tesla's new novelty tequila was originally going to be called \"Teslaquila,\" but because of strict rules in Mexico surrounding the drink it had to settle for the less punny \"Tesla Tequila,\" <a href=\"https://www.theverge.com/21578576/tesla-tequila-name-bottle-branding-elon-musk-mexico\">The Verge</a> reports.</p><p>Tesla — which has a history of launching novelty merchandise, including <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-sells-red-satin-tesla-short-shorts-2020-7\">red satin short shorts</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-limited-edition-surfboards-2018-7\">$1,500 surfboards</a> — in November <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-tequila-elon-musk-electric-car-company-drink-2020-11\">launched Tesla Tequila for $250 a bottle</a>. The drink sold out within hours, and resellers even started <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-tequila-teslaquila-resold-online-ebay-empty-bottle-2020-11\">hawking the empty bottles for up to $700 on eBay</a>.</p><p>Tesla CEO Elon Musk first used the word Teslaquila in a jokey April 2018 tweet that imagined Tesla had gone bankrupt.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Elon Musk  (@elonmusk) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/980566116614291456?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">April 1, 2018</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>A few months later he seemed set on turning the joke into a piece of branding, as in October 2018 he <a href=\"https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/1050788043907448834\">tweeted</a>: \"Teslaquila coming soon.\"</p><p>This proved more difficult than expected. Tequila is a designation of origin, meaning to call your drink tequila you have to produce it in Mexico and follow certain rules. According to The Verge, the company's effort to brand its drink Teslaquila was blocked by Mexico's Tequila Regulatory Council.</p><p>\"[The] name 'Teslaquila' evokes the word Tequila ... (and) Tequila is a protected word,\" the council argued in <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-tequila-teslaquila-mexican-industry-2018-11\">November 2018</a>.</p><p>The council head, Martín Muñoz, said the name Teslaquila could cause confusion about the drink's origin, and in February 2019 the council filed an objection. Essentially, if Tesla wanted to make a tequila, it had to use the word tequila without changing it so as to avoid diluting the brand.</p><p>A month later, the Mexican Institute of Industrial Property ruled Teslaquila could not be registered.</p><p>Musk's team argued back in July, saying the name was just the Tesla brand name with \"quila\" added on — but this didn't convince the regulator, which in January handed down its ruling.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/electric-car-race-over-tesla-won-musk-knows-doesnt-matter-2020-8?r=ih-sub\">Winning the electric-car race is just the beginning of Elon Musk's plan for Tesla</a></em></p><p>There don't seem to be hard feelings, however, as Muñoz told The Verge: \"Today the tequila industry has someone as important as Elon Musk representing it. This is, without a doubt, a benefit to all the tequila producers because he is giving his image as an important businessman and he is showing he wants to comply with the rules of this industry.</p><p>\"We welcome Elon Musk and the Tesla tequila brand.\"</p><p>Tesla Tequila is made by a California-based label called Nosotros Tequila, which per Reuters belongs to the Mexican producer Casa Maestri.</p><p>Tesla's product-design officer, Javier Verdura, did not comment on Tesla Tequila's timeline when contacted by The Verge, but he did say the company had trouble finding a manufacturer that could make the distinctive lightning-bolt-shaped bottle.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc5ced050e71a00115581b6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"NTV logo\" height=\"2661\" width=\"3548\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Sergei Karpukhin/ Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Russian state broadcaster NTV aired an attempted satirical segment over the weekend with a Russian actress in blackface portraying former US president Barack Obama in blackface.</li>\n<li>The host, Tigran Keosayan, asks a series of racist questions about Obama's new book, \"A Promised Land,\" while the actress in blackface screams \"Black Lives Matter\" and says her family can't write.</li>\n<li>The host's wife, Russian-state controlled network RT's editor-in-chief Margarita Simonyan, defended the skit and said that due to her husband's ethnic Armenian background, he jokes about marginalized communities.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Kremlin-affiliated TV station NTV aired a racist program over the weekend featuring a Russian actress in blackface, apparently posing as former US president Barack Obama.</p><p>In 2008, Obama was the first Black man to be elected as president of the United States — more than 140 <a href=\"http://content.time.com/time/nation/article/0,8599,1857222,00.html\">years after the Emancipation Proclamation</a> was signed by President Abraham Lincoln, which effectively ended 400 years of the enslavement of Black men, women, and children in the United States.</p><p>Blackface is part of that enduring legacy of slavery and racism in the US, a remnant of minstrel shows, in which white Americans painted their face black to mock black people with racist caricatures in the 1800s.</p><p>The racist skit appeared on NTV's \"Mezhdunarodnaya Pilorama\" or \"International Sawmill,\" a satirical show with Tigran Keosayan as the host. In the segment, a Russian actress appears as Obama, wearing blackface and baggy clothes and a bandana and gesturing in an attempt to mimic rappers.</p><p>The segment ran about a minute and a half and Keosayan promotes it as an interview with Obama about his new book, \"A Promised Land.\"&#160;</p><p>\"We now go live to the dark side of America's history, Barack Obama,\" Keosayan says, introducing the actress in blackface.</p><p>The actress immediately chants \"Black lives matter!\" to which Keosayan asks her to stop shouting and says that racism does not exist in Russia. Keosayan then continues with racist questions about the book.</p><p>Keosayan asks the actress if she is proud of her book, to which she says, \"Of course.\" Keosayan then asks, \"Because none of your relatives have written books?\" to which she replies, \"Because none of my relatives that came before me could write.\"&#160;</p><p>Keosayan then tells her she should have been a rapper and not a US president, and the actress starts to rap for the host.&#160;</p><p>NTV did not immediately respond to a request for comment.</p><p>Margarita Simonyan, the editor in chief of the Russian-state controlled network RT and Keosayan's partner, defended the skit on Twitter, and additional reporting from the Moscow Times uncovered that the pair <a href=\"https://www.themoscowtimes.com/2020/11/30/obama-blackface-skit-on-kremlin-funded-tv-sparks-outrage-a72176\">were co-writers.</a> Simonyan argued that Keosayan's background as an ethnic Armenian and self-deprecating humor about his background meant that the new skit was not over the top.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Alexey Navalny  (@navalny) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1333116137433931778?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">November 29, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>&#160;</p><p>Russian opposition figure Alexei Navalny <a href=\"https://twitter.com/navalny/status/1333116137433931778?s=21\">posted</a> on Twitter, bashing the segment and sarcastically saying that he couldn't \"ignore another masterpiece\" from the pair, also alleging that the two writers profit heavily from the skit and have sent their daughter to study in the US.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Facebook CEO Mark Zuckerberg.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters/Alan Freed; Tom Williams/CQ Roll Call</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Mark Zuckerberg said in a livestreamed interview with Dr. Anthony Fauci that Facebook had been in touch with the incoming Biden administration about how it might help with the coronavirus response.</li>\n<li>Zuckerberg said Facebook was planning a \"push around authoritative information on vaccines,\" though he did not elaborate on what this would look like.</li>\n<li>The Financial Times reported last week that Facebook was href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Facebook is trying to collaborate with President-elect Joe Biden, its chief executive said Monday.</p><p>During a <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/zuck/videos/10112595016437891\">livestreamed interview</a> with Dr. Anthony Fauci, CEO Mark Zuckerberg said Facebook had made contact with the incoming Biden administration about ways it could help with the coronavirus response.</p><p>This included promoting \"authoritative information\" on vaccines, he said.</p><p>\"Our team at Facebook has already reached out to the incoming administration to help with the COVID response in any way that we can. I'm sure there will be a few important things that we can do together,\" Zuckerberg said.</p><p>\"We're already planning a push around authoritative information on vaccines,\" he added.</p><p>Zuckerberg did not elaborate on what this \"push\" would look like.</p><p>Zuckerberg's comments tally with a <a href=\"https://www.ft.com/content/18a95526-3af9-4545-9d77-b3a0d7a7640a\">Financial Times</a> report from last week that Facebook was planning to roll out features promoting accurate information about vaccines and climate change as a way of getting on Biden's good side.</p><p>The president-elect has already shown signs he will <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-bill-russo-facebook-misinformation-social-media-attack-2020-11\">come down hard on Facebook over misinformation</a> on its platform.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/heres-how-biden-harris-could-crack-down-on-tech-advertising-2020-11?r=ih-sub\">5 experts predict how a Biden administration could crack down on the advertising and tech industries</a></em></p><p>Company sources told the Financial Times that Facebook was considering putting a banner at the top of its site encouraging users to get a COVID-19 vaccine.</p><p>In October, the social-media giant <a href=\"https://about.fb.com/news/2020/10/supporting-public-health-experts-vaccine-efforts/\">launched a new \"preventative health tool\"</a> that directed users toward information about getting flu shots.</p><p>Both <a href=\"https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/health-55129336#:~:text=Moderna%20is%20filing%20for%20US,to%20recommend%20for%20roll%20out.\">Moderna</a> and <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/11/20/health/pfizer-covid-vaccine.html\">Pfizer</a> have filed for emergency authorization of their COVID-19 vaccines, so it's possible Facebook will roll out something similar once vaccines become available to the public.</p><p>Facebook also announced in October it was changing its policy to ban ads that discourage people from getting vaccinated.</p><p>The platform does not fully ban anti-vaccination — also known as \"anti-vaxx\" — content, though in <a href=\"https://www.wired.com/story/facebook-anti-vaccine-crack-down/\">February</a> it said it would start making pages and groups that regularly promote anti-vaxx posts more difficult to find in its search results.</p><p>Imran Ahmed, the CEO of the Center for Countering Digital Hate campaign group, said Zuckerberg's announcement was not addressing the real problem.</p><p>\"Mr. Zuckerberg is deeply hypocritical to claim he is offering to help with the Coronavirus vaccine, when his companies, Facebook and Instagram, host the world's most renowned anti-vaxxers and amplify their toxic lies into tens of millions of users' timelines,\" Ahmed said.</p><p>Ahmed said if Facebook were serious about vaccine misinformation, it should remove prominent sources of misinformation from its platform. \"If Mark Zuckerberg really wanted to help, he could remove the identified pages and groups, some with hundreds of thousands or millions of followers, which spread lies about vaccines, as laid out clearly in <a href=\"https://252f2edd-1c8b-49f5-9bb2-cb57bb47e4ba.filesusr.com/ugd/f4d9b9_7aa1bf9819904295a0493a013b285a6b.pdf\">our report on the Anti-Vaxx Industry,</a>\" Ahmed said.</p><div
