One of the most pressing issues in need of attention is the rising number of shootings. Across the country,<a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/tommybeer/2020/08/02/shootings-and-gun-deaths-continue-to-rise-at-alarming-rate-in-large-us-cities/?sh=719a66a86f0f\"> shootings have skyrocketed</a> this year, especially in large cities, and even more disturbing are the number of children caught in the crossfire.&#160;</p><p>The homicide rate in Philadelphia is<a href=\"https://www.phillypolice.com/crime-maps-stats/\"> 38% higher</a> than last year, and by the end of the summer, nearly 100 children under the age of 18 had been<a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2020/08/07/us/philly-shootings-children-trnd/index.html#:~:text=(CNN)%20At%20least%2098%20individuals,under%20the%20age%20of%2010.&text=Police%20data%20shows%20nine%20of%20the%20shootings%20were%20fatal.tal.\"> shot</a>. Compared with last year, New York City had nearly doubled their shootings and shooting fatalities as of September, with over<a href=\"https://www.nbcnewyork.com/news/local/crime-and-courts/nycs-surge-in-gun-violence-sees-spike-in-kid-teen-and-young-adult-victims/2514840/\"> 50 children shot</a>.&#160;</p><p>Murder and shooting rates are up nearly 50% in Chicago and in the recent weeks,<a href=\"https://chicago.suntimes.com/crime/2020/10/31/21543106/chicago-shootings-gun-violence-weekend-homicide-october-30-november-1\"> over 30 people were shot</a> in the span of just a few days. As of October, nearly 50 children in Chicago were victims of firearm violence this year.</p><p>As a pediatric emergency medicine physician in Chicago, I feel as if we are watching the next mass shooting unfold before our eyes. We need to take this moment with new White House leadership to make progress on regulating guns for the sake of our children.&#160;</p><h2>Guns are turning into a public health emergency</h2><p>Firearm injuries (15%) are the second-leading<a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/injury/wisqars/LeadingCauses.html\"> cause of death</a> for US children. Car crashes (20%) are the No. 1 cause of death in children ages 1-19. Yet, federal funding for pediatric firearm injuries is only<a href=\"https://www.healthaffairs.org/doi/abs/10.1377/hlthaff.2019.00476?journalCode=hlthaff\"> funded at 3%</a> of what it should be based on its mortality burden (how many deaths can be attributed to this phenomenon) compared with other causes of death. A<a href=\"https://jamanetwork.com/journals/jama/fullarticle/2595514\"> study</a> in 2017 found that, compared with other leading causes of death, gun violence was one of the least researched in relation to its mortality rate.&#160;&#160;</p><p>Research on the dangers and health consequences of firearms was almost completely banned until recently because of the Dickey Amendment. The<a href=\"https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5993413/\"> amendment</a>, passed in 1996 as part of a larger <a href=\"https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5993413/\">spending bill</a> and backed by the National Rifle Association, restricted the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention from funding anything that \"advocated or promoted gun control.\" Many interpreted this directive to include research on gun violence, which effectively led to the shutdown of any meaningful firearms research. We need to make up for lost time. In December 2019, for the first time in 20 years, Congress approved<a href=\"https://www.ajmc.com/view/gun-violence-research-receives-federal-funding-for-first-time-in-20-years\"> $25 million</a> dollars for gun violence research.&#160;&#160;</p><p>This is a start, but it is not nearly enough.</p><p>Prevention efforts also are needed to stop shooting injuries and fatalities to children. Most children's firearm injuries involve guns stored in the<a href=\"https://jamanetwork.com/journals/jamapediatrics/fullarticle/347593\"> home of the victim</a> or that of a friend or relative. An estimated<a href=\"https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s11524-018-0261-7\"> 4.6 million children</a> live in homes with guns that are stored unsafely, unlocked, and loaded.&#160;</p><p>A recent<a href=\"https://jamanetwork.com/journals/jamapediatrics/article-abstract/2761305#:~:text=Child%20access%20prevention%20(CAP)%20laws%20are%20state%2Dlevel%20laws,firearms%20in%20households%20with%20minors.&text=We%20conducted%20a%20state%2Dlevel,years%20from%201991%20to%202016.016.\"> study</a> found more stringent laws that hold gun owners liable for unsafe storage of firearms were associated with decreased pediatric firearm deaths.&#160; Currently, only half of states have laws that regulate any accountability of gun owners for safe firearm storage, and these laws vary in strictness.</p><p>The threat of guns is ever-present. We have been bombarded by images of rifle and handgun-toting Trump supporters attempting intimidation at<a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-election-reaction-idUSKBN27M2ND\"> voting sites</a> and<a href=\"https://gunsandamerica.org/story/20/07/30/guns-anti-police-violence-protests-aurora-colorado/\"> protests</a>.&#160; These self-proclaimed militiamen are domestic terrorists pushing the normalcy of carrying and flaunting guns in public. These are the images our children absorb. They are images endorsed and propagated by the soon-to-be former president of our country.&#160;</p><p>The Brady Campaign, a national nonprofit gun control advocacy group,<a href=\"https://twitter.com/KrisB_Brown/status/1325123498256207872?s=20\"> announced</a> that now President-elect Joe Biden and Vice President-elect Kamala Harris were the strongest gun violence protection ticket in our country's history. Let's take advantage of this momentum to make homes and streets safer for our children and debunk the normalization of deadly firearms in the public imagination.</p><p>Restriction of firearm rights is a sensitive topic in the US. There are political implications and emotions not present when we discuss other health issues.&#160; However, safe firearm storage reduces pediatric gun injuries and deaths.&#160;</p><p>When the election has ceased to consume all of our attention and headlines in the next days and&#160; weeks, we must get back to work planning for how to protect our children from ongoing gun injuries and violence.&#160;&#160;</p><p><em>Dr. Sheryl Yanger, a Public Voices Fellow of The OpEd Project, is an assistant professor of pediatrics (emergency medicine) at Northwestern University Feinberg School of Medicine.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 22:27:43","updatedTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:43","title":"How to share a fleet in a tweet on Twitter's mobile app","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-share-a-fleet-in-a-tweet","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f77601274fe5b0018a8ec7e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"twitter logo\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>It&#39;s easy to tweet out (certain) fleets you&#39;ve made on Twitter.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jaap Arriens/NurPhoto via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>You can share a Twitter fleet as a tweet, but only if you were the creator of the original fleet.</li>\n<li>Twitter's fleets feature allows users to share ephemeral images, video, text, and share tweets.</li>\n<li>To share a fleet as a tweet, your fleet has to be a still image or text-based fleet; it can't be a video.&#160;</li>\n<li>The fleets feature is currently only available within the Twitter mobile app.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\"><strong>Visit Business Insider's Tech Reference library for more stories</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/twitter\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Twitter's</a> latest feature, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/fleets\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">fleets</a>, allows users to share ephemeral images, video, text and tweets in a story-like format popularized by Snapchat and Instagram.&#160;</p><p>The social media company rolled out the fleets feature in November 2020 to all US users, but so far it is only available within the Twitter app, not yet on desktop.&#160;</p><p>Tweets can be fleeted — and fleets can also be tweeted. However, you can only tweet out fleets you've made from your own account. The fleet also cannot be a video file; it has to be a still image or text-based fleet.&#160;</p><p>Here's how to share a fleet in a tweet.&#160;</p><h2><strong>How to share a fleet in a tweet using the Twitter app</strong></h2><p><strong>1.</strong> Open the Twitter app on your device. The fleets feature is only available within the Twitter mobile app.&#160;</p><p><strong>2.</strong> At the top of the page you will see icons with various users' profile photos — this is where you can find your fleets and other users' fleets. Fleets can also be found by going to a user's profile page and tapping on their profile photo. A blue circle will appear around the fleets you have not yet seen.&#160;</p><p><strong>3.</strong> Select your profile image in the top left corner of the app. This will take you to your current fleets. If you don't have any fleets currently posted, it will take you to your camera roll.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc550ea50e71a001155808c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Fleet_1\" height=\"800\" width=\"1019\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tap on your profile icon to go to your fleets.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Meira Gebel/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>4.</strong> Select the fleet you wish to share. If you haven't yet used the fleet feature, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-post-fleet-on-twitter\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">here's how</a>.</p><p><strong>5.</strong> Once you've found the fleet of yours you wish to tweet, tap the down arrow in the top right corner.&#160;</p><p><strong>6.</strong> In the pop-up window, select \"Tweet this.\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc5517350e71a0011558095?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Fleet2\" height=\"1626\" width=\"819\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tap the down arrow in the top right corner of your fleet and select &#34;Tweet this.&#34;\n<p class=\"copyright\">Meira Gebel/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>7.</strong> Type a comment to accompany the fleet, if you wish. When you're ready, select \"Tweet.\"&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc551f550e71a0011558099?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Fleet3\" height=\"1633\" width=\"822\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Write a comment and tap &#34;Tweet.&#34;\n<p class=\"copyright\">Meira Gebel/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>8.</strong> The fleet will only be available for 24 hours, but the tweet including the fleet will be visible for longer.&#160;&#160;</p><h2><strong>Related coverage from&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">Tech Reference</a>:</strong></h2><ul><li><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-post-fleet-on-twitter\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">How to post a fleet on Twitter in 2 ways, and share temporary text, pictures, or videos<br></a></h3></li><li><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-long-can-a-fleet-be-on-twitter\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">How long can a fleet be on Twitter? 22:27:43","updatedTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:43","title":"Topshop owner Arcadia falls into administration, putting more than 13,000 jobs at risk. It's the UK's biggest corporate casualty of the COVID-19 crisis so far.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/arcadia-group-administration-topshop-philip-green-covid-19-2020-12","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc6082850e71a00115581cd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Simon Dawson:Reuters.JPG\" height=\"2653\" width=\"3538\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Simon Dawson/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The Arcadia Group, which owns British fashion brands including Topshop, Dorothy Perkins, and Miss Selfridge, has fallen into administration, Deloitte confirmed Monday night.</li>\n<li>This puts more than 13,000 jobs at risk, though no redundancies have been announced yet.</li>\n<li>The company's CEO said COVID-19 was to blame. The pandemic has caused Arcadia's stores to close in two national lockdowns.</li>\n<li>But rival fast fashion retailers were already attracting the Arcadia Group's customers before the pandemic.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>British tycoon Philip Green's Arcadia fashion group has collapsed into administration, putting more than 13,000 jobs at risk and becoming the country's biggest corporate casualty of the COVID-19 pandemic so far.</p><p>Deloitte said late on Monday it had been appointed&#160;Arcadia's administrator and would seek buyers for the group's brands: Topshop, Topman, Dorothy Perkins, Wallis, Miss Selfridge, Evans, Burton and Outfit.</p><p>Arcadia's close to 500 stores would continue to trade, its online platforms would remain operational, and supplies to concession partners would continue, Deloitte said.</p><p>No redundancies were being immediately announced, it added.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-fashion-boss-says-more-luxury-brands-want-sell-amazon-2020-11?r=gd-sub\">Amazon's fashion chief told employees that 50 brands have inquired about selling in its new luxury store, as the company tries to shed counterfeit concerns</a></em></p><p>Green acquired Arcadia for £850 million ($1.14 billion) in 2002.</p><p>He had no immediate comment, but his CEO laid the blame for Arcadia's demise firmly on the pandemic.</p><p>\"In the face of the most difficult trading conditions we have ever experienced, the obstacles we encountered were far too severe,\" said Ian Grabiner.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/uk-retail-sales-recovery-is-deceptive-and-clothes-hardest-hit-2020-9\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"2276b22df83348fd324ba52c124e42fc\">Apparel is one of retail sectors hit the most by the pandemic</a>. Arcadia's brands have been hit by two national lockdowns, which forced non-essential businesses, including clothing stores, to shut, alongside falling demand for footwear and formal clothing.</p><p>Senior British minister Michael Gove said it was \"tragic\" but that mistakes had been made by management.</p><p>\"I'm not going to criticise any individual but there's been a lot of reporting that points out some of the missteps that have been made by the management there,\" he told Sky News Tuesday.</p><p>While COVID-19 lockdowns pushed&#160;Arcadia&#160;over the edge, it has struggled in recent years, underinvesting and failing to keep pace with competitors in an increasingly online retail sector.</p><p>Its brands were squeezed between the likes of Inditex's Zara, H&#38;M, and Primark, and online-only players ASOS and Boohoo.</p><p>\"Arcadia's brands have been slow to diversify into other countries or to make an exciting online offering and have not kept pace with the contemporary fashion offerings of the online-only competitors,\" Dr Gordon Fletcher, a retail expert from the University of Salford Business School, told Business Insider.</p><p>Arcadia's share of the UK clothing market has slumped to 2.7% in 2020 from 4.5% in 2015, according to figures GlobalData shared with Business Insider.</p><p>A restructuring deal was approved by creditors last year, cutting rents and closing stores, but proved only a temporary respite.</p><h2>Sale process</h2><p>\"We will be rapidly seeking expressions of interest and expect to identify one or more buyers to ensure the future success of the businesses,\" said Matt Smith, Deloitte's joint administrator.</p><p>Mike Ashley's Frasers Group said on Monday it was interested in participating in any&#160;Arcadia&#160;sale process.</p><p>Topshop, once the go-to destination for teenagers and fashion lovers, is regarded by analysts as&#160;Arcadia's most attractive asset.</p><p>Media reports have also identified Marks &#38; Spencer, Next, and Boohoo, as well as private equity players, as potential bidders for individual brands. All three companies declined to comment.</p><p>Arcadia's collapse could have a knock-on impact on the future of department store chain Debenhams, which is already in administration and employs 12,000.</p><p>Arcadia&#160;is one of Debenhams' biggest concession holders.</p><h2>Pension funds deficit</h2><p>Arcadia's workforce also faces uncertainty over a deficit in the company's pension fund, estimated by analysts at about £350 million ($470 million).</p><p>As part of last year's restructuring, Arcadia agreed to provide £210 million ($281 million) of security over property assets to the pension schemes, while Tina Green, Philip's wife and the ultimate owner of Arcadia, agreed to contribute £100 million ($134 million) to the schemes over three years.</p><p>\"Philip Green should do the right thing and fill the&#160;Arcadia&#160;pension deficit,\" said opposition Labour Party leader Keir Starmer.</p><p>If Green does not pay up, Arcadia's 10,000 pension scheme members should still receive the bulk of their entitlement through the government's lifeboat scheme, the Pension Protection Fund.</p><p>British Business secretary Alok Sharma said the administrators had three months to file a report on the conduct of Arcadia's directors with The Insolvency Service, which will determine whether a full investigation is required.</p><h2>Philip Green</h2><p>Much of the group's controversy comes from its chairman, Sir Philip Green. The business tycoon paid out a £1.2 billion ($1.6 billion) dividend to his wife, who is Arcadia's registered owner, just three years after he bought the group for £850 million ($1.1 billion).</p><p>Green also owned the department store chain British Home Stores, which he infamously sold for just £1 ($1.33) in 2015. The chain went bankrupt the next year in&#160;<a href=\"https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/business-36437445\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"1f8c79aa95f59812b234f90e61d2c13e\">the UK's biggest retail collapse since 2008</a>, causing the closure of 163 stores and the loss of around 11,000 jobs.</p><p>In June 2019, Green was&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/topshop-uk-retailer-philip-green-assault-charges-us-2019-6\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"adfce85f40a43d58ba32daef5e482942\">charged with four counts of misdemeanor assault</a>&#160;after a fitness instructor reportedly accused him of unwanted groping in Arizona. Just months before that, a member of the UK parliament named him as the subject of&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/topshop-billionaire-owner-philip-green-accused-of-sexual-misconduct-2018-10\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"1528a70a39e90b189dc5b630d411f63b\">several sexual harassment, racial abuse, and bullying allegations</a>.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/arcadia-group-administration-topshop-philip-green-covid-19-2020-12'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a The famed investor's company <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-experts-analyze-strategy-caution-deals-2020-10?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">responded to the backlash</a> by announcing more than $35 billion worth of stock purchases, buybacks, and deals last quarter.</p><p>Berkshire spent $17.6 billion on equities in the three months to September 30, its <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-q3-earnings-stock-purchases-buybacks-2020-11-1029777502\">latest earnings show</a>. That figure includes its <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-bank-of-america-buying-years-pay-off-experts-2020-8-1029477087#\">$2 billion-plus purchase</a> of Bank of America stock, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-approach-200-percent-gain-snowflake-stock-2020-11-1029849372\">$735 million investment</a> in Snowflake, and roughly <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-invests-pfizer-merck-abbvie-pharmaceutical-stocks-2020-11-1029808269\">$5 billion bet</a> on AbbVie, Bristol Myers Squibb, Merck, and Pfizer.</p><p><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Read More:</em></strong><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">&#160;</em><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-covid-recovery-value-rotation-undervalued-rbc-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-covid-recovery-value-rotation-undervalued-rbc-2020-11\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">Buy these 10 stocks set to soar and smash Wall Street's expectations in the recovery from COVID-19, RBC says</a></em></p><p>Berkshire also disclosed in August that it had <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-reveals-6-billion-investment-5-japanese-companies-2020-8-1029546397?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest#est#\">built 5% stakes</a> in five Japanese trading companies over the preceding 12 months, at a cost of about $5 billion. Moreover, it secured regulatory permission to not disclose one of the stocks in its portfolio last quarter, suggesting it's <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-buying-secret-stock-revealed-coming-weeks-2020-11-1029813523\">building a secret position</a>.</p><p>Buffett and his team snapped up Berkshire shares as well. They repurchased $9 billion worth in the three-month period, smashing their previous quarterly buyback record of $5.1 billion.</p><p>Berkshire's bosses struck a couple of deals too. They <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-strike-10-billion-deal-dominion-energy-2020-7-1029368062#\">shook hands</a> on acquiring most of Dominion Energy's natural-gas assets in exchange for $4 billion in cash and taking on $5.7 billion of the energy group's debt.</p><p><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Read More:&#160;</em></strong><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/goldman-sachs-esg-trends-markets-climate-investing-stock-sustainability-social-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/goldman-sachs-esg-trends-markets-climate-investing-stock-sustainability-social-2020-11\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">A top equity portfolio strategist at Goldman Sachs shares his four essential ESG trends that you need to be thinking about</a></em></p><p>They also <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-basics-scripps-snowflake-barrick-gold-2020-9-1029626458#\">agreed to help finance</a> Scripps' acquisition of ION Media, handing the broadcaster $600 million in exchange for preferred shares and $300 million worth of stock warrants.</p><h2>Buying and selling</h2><p>Buffett's company spent nearly $18 billion on stocks last quarter, but it also sold $12.8 billion worth. For example, it <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-built-8-billion-jpmorgan-stake-slashed-2020-11-1029846193\">dumped more than 95%</a> of its JPMorgan stock, almost halved its <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-cuts-wells-fargo-stake-17-years-2020-9-1029566739#\">remaining Wells Fargo stake</a>, and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-sold-costco-stake-despite-praising-retailer-2020-11-1029826795\">exited its Costco position</a> after more than 20 years.</p><p>Still, the combination of Berkshire's $4.8 billion in net stock purchases, $9 billion worth of buybacks, and more than $10 billion in deals should assuage any doubts that Buffett and his team are willing to splash their cash.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a outbreak","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/north-dakota-health-officer-insulted-booed-coronavirus-surge-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc55bc350e71a00115580d3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"north dakota coronavirus\" height=\"2928\" width=\"3904\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Nurse Deb Grabo, wearing an air-purifying Guan/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>North Dakota is experiencing a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fargo-mayor-tim-mahoney-mandatory-mask-mandate-bring-cases-down-2020-10\">devastating surge</a> in COVID-19 cases: One in 10 residents has gotten sick.</li>\n<li>Yet public-health officers say they <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/doctors-health-workers-us-coronavirus-hotspots-villainized-2020-11\">face antagonism</a> from the public and other government leaders when they attempt to promote social distancing and mask wearing.</li>\n<li>One North Dakota health official said she was called a \"Nazi\" and \"tyrant\" after calling for restrictions to curb the virus' spread.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>One out of every 10 people in North Dakota has gotten the coronavirus. The state's total of COVID-19 deaths has jumped more than 200% in the last two months.</p><p>But Renae Moch, the public-health director for Bismarck and Burleigh County, said that despite these numbers, she faces a cruel irony: Messages of hate and vitriol from the people whose lives she's trying to save.</p><p>Moch said local residents called her a \"Nazi\" and \"tyrant\" when she pushed for a mask mandate this fall. Burleigh County has the <a href=\"https://www.health.nd.gov/diseases-conditions/coronavirus/north-dakota-coronavirus-cases\">highest number of cases per capita in the state</a>, and the third-highest total number of deaths.</p><p>\"Let me tell you, I'm the furthest thing from a tyrant,\" Moch told Business Insider. \"They say I'm lying about the dangers of COVID. Why would I want to do that? Nothing could be further from the truth.\"</p><p>She added that if doctors and other health experts are telling you that masks can save lives and that the virus is dangerous, \"that's who you need to trust and the information you should move forward with.\"</p><h2>From 'we're all in this together' to hate mail</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc55b08037cbd0018612f73?format=jpeg\" alt=\"north dakota coronavirus\" height=\"3598\" width=\"4797\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A woman wearing a mask stands near the Sanford Medical Center in Bismarck, North Dakota, October 26, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bing Guan/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>At the beginning of North Dakota's outbreak, Moch said, \"people were supportive\" of the work she and and other experts were doing.</p><p>\"Then we reopened and people went back to their routines, and we didn't get hit that hard. So people lost faith in public-health measures,\" she said.&#160;</p><p>Like many other health officers, Moch has advocated for mask requirements, more testing and contact tracing, and stronger messaging about the need for isolation and quarantines. She's part of the Burleigh-Morton COVID-19 Task Force, a group that makes recommendations to lawmakers in both counties. When cases started to surge in the late summer, the task force suggested a mask mandate and restrictions on some businesses.</p><p>Then things got ugly.</p><p>\"The hearts in the windows and the love and the 'we're all in this together' that was in March has faded away to vulgarity and rude untruths that is just beyond my comprehension,\" Moch <a href=\"https://bismarcktribune.com/news/local/bismarck/harassment-personal-attacks-directed-at-local-public-health-directors-amid-pandemic/article_8cbd6033-c01b-57fe-a90e-34a7dcbb8f62.html\">told the Bismark Tribune</a> in September.</p><p>Because of her high-visibility role, Moch said, she's become a focal point. People have protested outside her office, holding signs and booing, and written nasty messages to her on social media.</p><p>\"There's a crowd that hates me and sends hate mail,\" she said.</p><h2>'It's been challenging trying to be the voice of public health'</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc55b12037cbd0018612f74?format=jpeg\" alt=\"north dakota coronavirus\" height=\"2624\" width=\"3498\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Nurse Dana Simmers&#39; glasses fog up as she dons an N95 mask before her shift at a drive-thru testing site at the Bismarck Event Center in North Dakota.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bing Guan/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Deborah Birx, the White House coronavirus response coordinator, said in October that Bismarck had <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/virus-outbreak-health-fargo-north-dakota-f1389b4e5e7725846bc50309c4d1b0bc\">the worst COVID-19 protocols</a> she'd seen anywhere in the US. Yet in city commission meetings, locals have continued to ardently condemn mask requirements and business closures.</p><p>\"I've personally, just in the last few weeks, experienced the loss of two close family friends due to consequences of COVID,\" one resident said at an October meeting. Then she went on to explain that despite those deaths, her anti-mask stance hadn't changed.</p><p>\"I cannot... blindly follow the herd and put a piece of cloth over my face,\" she said.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc55b1950e71a00115580ce?format=jpeg\" alt=\"north dakota coronavirus\" height=\"2663\" width=\"3551\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>North Dakota State University students study inside the school&#39;s Memorial Union in Fargo, North Dakota, October 25, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bing Guan/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>In that particular meeting, Moch and two doctors answered medical questions from city commissioners for hours. It was a low point, she said.</p><p>\"The two experts were challenged over and over. It's embarrassing,\" Moch said.</p><p>After the meeting, she added, Moch found her phone flooded with texts from concerned witnesses: \"I can't believe you're still working your job after that,\" she recalled the messages saying.</p><p>\"It's been challenging trying to be the voice of public health and tell commissioners these mitigation measures have been around for very long time,\" Moch said, adding, \"when they hear business shutdowns, social distancing, masks ... everyone has to come back with a study that discounts what we say.\"</p><h2>'It's like the pandemic doesn't exist'</h2><p>According to a poll commissioned by the North Dakota Newspaper Association, <a href=\"https://bismarcktribune.com/news/local/health/quarter-of-north-dakotans-know-someone-who-has-died-of-covid-19/article_8b95bb6a-669a-50fd-aa1c-233210384686.html\">24% of North Dakotans</a> reported knowing someone who had died from the coronavirus.</p><p>Currently, the statewide test-positivity rate (the portion of coronavirus tests coming back positive) hovers around 8.5%. Anthony Fauci, director of the National Institute of Allergy and Infectious Diseases, has said the rate should ideally sit below 3%.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc55b0e50e71a00115580cd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"north dakota coronavirus\" height=\"2671\" width=\"3565\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A person receives a coronavirus throat swab test in Bismarck, North Dakota.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bing Guan/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>North Dakota Gov. Doug Burgum issued a statewide mask mandate in mid-November in response to the state's case surge, but <a href=\"https://bismarcktribune.com/news/local/health/quarter-of-north-dakotans-know-someone-who-has-died-of-covid-19/article_8b95bb6a-669a-50fd-aa1c-233210384686.html\">sheriff's departments</a> and <a href=\"https://www.grandforksherald.com/news/education/6770949-North-Dakota-schools-may-be-sanctioned-for-violating-statewide-mask-mandate\">school districts</a> from multiple counties have said they won't enforce the order.&#160;</p><p>\"What is the point of me trying all of this if nobody cares?\" Moch said. \"Here it's just like the pandemic doesn't exist.\"</p><div rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.ft.com/content/21f16d65-803d-4b2f-818a-5a1b7c712481?shareType=nongift\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">Financial Times</a></strong><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\">.</strong></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Two drugmakers with leading COVID-19 vaccines said Tuesday they have asked the European Union to approve their shots.</p><p>After submitting an application on Monday to the European Medicines Agency (EMA), Pfizer and BioNTech said the EU regulator accepted the application on Tuesday, per the <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/pfizer-biontech-file-for-covid-19-vaccine-approval-in-europe-11606816904\">Wall Street Journal</a>.</p><p>Moderna has also submitted its EU application.</p><p>The two vaccines were supposed to be assessed December 22 but this has been pushed back by the EU's regulator, according to documents seen by the <a href=\"https://www.ft.com/content/21f16d65-803d-4b2f-818a-5a1b7c712481?shareType=nongift\">Financial Times</a>.</p><p>The EMA's scientific committee will decide whether data from trials — which suggest the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-says-coronavirus-vaccine-effective-will-submit-to-fda-eua-2020-11?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">vaccine is 95% effective</a> —show that Pfizer's vaccine is safe and effective enough on or before December 29, it said in a press release.</p><p>A decision on that date would mean that distribution of the vaccine is unlikely to kick off by the end of 2020.</p><p>EU regulators may not decide on Moderna's jab before January 12, per the FT.</p><p>Pfizer and BioNTech said they hoped to begin vaccinating in 2020.</p><p>\"If EMA concludes that the benefits of the vaccine candidate outweigh its risks in protecting against COVID‑19, it will recommend granting a CMA (conditional marketing authorization) that could potentially enable use of BNT162b2 in Europe before the end of 2020,\" they said in a joint statement.</p><p>The drugmakers submitted an application for conditional marketing authorization (CMA), which is a fast-track for approval. For this to be granted, data from the companies' trials must show that the benefits of the vaccine outweigh any potential risks.</p><p>If the EMA grants the vaccine a CMA, the drugmakers still have to provide more data from ongoing or new studies within a certain timeframe.</p><p>Pfizer and BioNTech's application to the EMA comes after the companies applied for authorization in the US on November 20 and the UK on November 23.</p><p>Pfizer's coronavirus vaccine candidate was 95% effective at protecting people against COVID-19 in its late-stage trial, the pharmaceutical giant <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-says-coronavirus-vaccine-effective-will-submit-to-fda-eua-2020-11?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">announced</a> November 18.</p><p>The biotech company Moderna said two days before that its vaccine <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-works-to-prevent-covid-19-company-says-2020-11\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"882d1305389caae887a4c1a5df685d16\">appeared to be 94.5% effective against COVID-19</a>, based on a preliminary analysis of its late-stage trial.</p><p>Moderna <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-covid-vaccine-emergency-use-authorization-fda-2020-11?utmSource=twitter&utmContent=referral&utmTerm=topbar&referrer=twitter&r=US&IR=Ter&#38;r=US&#38;IR=T\">asked the Food and Drug Administration Monday</a> to authorize its coronavirus vaccine for emergency use.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5fc5da4d50e71a00115581b9?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"46b1b989f030f5a350333ee2e1bad4a2","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn12@2020_1/2020/12/01/14-28-11-871_546ad66d6bf85aff.webp","destWidth":1666,"destHeight":1250,"sourceBytes":96378,"destBytes":96378,"author":"aharoun@businessinsider.com (Azmi Haroun)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5fc5da22037cbd0018613057?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn92@2020_1/2020/12/01/14-28-10-303_cee8ed946c3704c9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn19@2020_6/2020/12/01/14-28-10-417_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=ozGi04HJnJY:lC-wLgzSdng:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn3@2020_2/2020/12/01/14-28-05-784_1f0659ab31ff670d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=ozGi04HJnJY:lC-wLgzSdng:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn74@2020_4/2020/12/01/14-28-04-990_685282573798ab6a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn100@2020_6/2020/12/01/14-28-08-006_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=ozGi04HJnJY:lC-wLgzSdng:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn19@2020_1/2020/12/01/14-28-07-378_1a1b957a52972eb2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/ozGi04HJnJY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn87@2020_1/2020/12/01/14-28-10-308_80e9a363dc3315be.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1606832863128},{"createdTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:43","updatedTime":"2020-12-01 22:27:43","title":"Leaked documents reveal China severely underreported coronavirus cases as the pandemic spread","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/china-underreported-covid-19-infections-cnn-report-2020-12","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fc6206b037cbd0018613089?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Xi Jinping\" height=\"992\" width=\"1985\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Chinese President Xi Jinping.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Noel Celis - Pool/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Leaked documents reveal that China significantly underreported the number of coronavirus cases in the early stages of the pandemic.</li>\n<li>Health data from Chinese health authorities leaked to CNN shows that officials in the Hubei province, where the virus is believed to have originated, failed to report thousands of new daily cases.</li>\n<li>On February 10 &#8212; when China reported 2,478 new cases &#8212; officials privately recorded 5,918 new cases, more than double the published figure.</li>\n<li>There is no evidence in the files that provide evidence that Chinese officials sought deliberately to conceal the true extent of the outbreak.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A tranche of leaked documents has revealed that China's government significantly underreported the number of coronavirus cases in the early stages of the pandemic.</p><p>An extensive set of health data<a href=\"https://www.google.com/url?sa=t&rct=j&q=&esrc=s&source=newssearch&cd=&cad=rja&uact=8&ved=0ahUKEwjXnI2d06ztAhURZcAKHV36DKcQxfQBCDIwAA&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.cnn.com%2F2020%2F11%2F30%2Fasia%2Fwuhan-china-covid-intl%2Findex.html&usg=AOvVaw1M6yKacBE4plSe7bxif6Watml&#38;usg=AOvVaw1M6yKacBE4plSe7bxif6Wa\">&#160;from Chinese health authorities leaked to CNN</a> shows that health officials in the Hubei province, where the virus is believed to have originated, failed to report thousands of new daily cases in the early stages of the pandemic.</p><p>On February 10 — <a href=\"http://assets.businessinsider.com/china-reports-108-new-coronavirus-deaths-on-feb-10-total-at-1016-2020-2\">when China reported 2,478 new cases</a> — officials privately recorded 5,918 new cases, more than double the published figure, per CNN.</p><p>The underreporting was exacerbated by a slow-turnaround in identifying cases. &#160;One of the leaked documents reveals that in early March the average time between an individual exhibiting symptoms and diagnosis was 23.3 days, CNN reported.</p><p>Experts have traced the origins of COVID-19 to China, and believe the virus <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-did-not-jump-wuhan-market-chinese-cdc-says-2020-5?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">almost certainly originated in Chinese bats</a> before passing to humans. The virus <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-outbreak-wuhan-timeline-earlier-than-officials-say-2020-4?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">appears to have been circulating</a> in the Chinese city of Wuhan in December and January before the first large outbreak was reported in a wet market there.</p><p>The incomplete data set, leaked to CNN by a whistleblower who said they work inside the Chinese health system, provides a large amount of data for February 10 and March 7, two days early on in the coronavirus outbreak as it began to spread across the world.</p><p>By March 7, health officials also appeared to still be underreporting the death toll by a significant margin. Per CNN, the <a href=\"https://edition.cnn.com/2020/11/30/asia/wuhan-china-covid-intl/index.html\">documents show</a> that the total death toll in Hubei was 3,456, while published figures suggested it was 2,986.</p><p>The documents also reveal that the early stages of the pandemic coincided with a significant reported influenza outbreak in Hubei with cases 20 times higher than the previous year. The flu outbreak was first identified in Wuhan in December and in particular in the cities of Yichang and Xianning, CNN reported.&#160;</p><p>There is no evidence in the files that provides evidence that Chinese officials sought deliberately to conceal the true extent of the coronavirus outbreak.</p><p>But the leak is nonetheless significant because it fuels allegations made by President Trump and others, that China sought to cover up the severity of the COVID-19 outbreak in its early stages and let it spread across the world.</p><p>A May 1 report by the US Department of Homeland Security, <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/bf685dcf52125be54e030834ab7062a8\">obtained by the Associated Press</a>, reportedly said that Chinese leaders \"intentionally concealed the severity\" of the coronavirus outbreak in January while it hoarded medical equipment.</p><p>It said that China failed to inform the World Health Organisation for weeks in January that the new coronavirus was highly infectious while at the same time significantly increasing imports of face masks and surgical gowns that could be used by health officials treating coronavirus patients.&#160;</p><p>China has consistently denied allegations that it intentionally covered coronavirus data, calling it \"<a href=\"https://www.google.com/search?client=safari&rls=en&ei=-TLGX6RmlcHyAt2AoMAI&q=china+denies+covering+up+coronavirus&oq=china+denies+covering+up+coronavirus&gs_lcp=CgZwc3ktYWIQAzoFCAAQkQI6DgguELEDEIMBEMcBEKMCOggIABCxAxCDAToLCC4QsQMQxwEQowI6AggAOgUIABCxAzoFCC4QsQM6BAgAEEM6BAguEEM6CgguEMcBEKMCEEM6CgguELEDEIMBEEM6BwgAELEDEEM6CggAELEDEIMBEEM6CgguEMkDEEMQkwI6AgguOgQIABAKOgsILhCxAxDHARCvAToICAAQsQMQyQM6CAguEMcBEK8BOgUIABDJAzoGCAAQFhAeOgUIIRCgAVCQM1jxWmC3W2gAcAB4AIABowGIAZkdkgEFMTUuMjCYAQCgAQGqAQdnd3Mtd2l6wAEB&sclient=psy-ab&ved=0ahUKEwjkxqC64KztAhWVoFwKHV0ACIgQ4dUDCAw&uact=5WVoFwKHV0ACIgQ4dUDCAw&#38;uact=5\">a calculated slur,</a>\" per Bloomberg.</p><p>Whistleblowers in Hubei <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/wuhan-doctor-chinese-sounded-alarm-coronavirus-outbreak-december-2020-3?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">have also claimed</a> they were prevented from speaking publicly about the coronavirus as it spread in December.</p><p>However, US intelligence <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-intel-local-officials-withheld-information-on-coronavirus-threat-nyt-2020-8?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">also reportedly indicates</a> that much of the Chinese government's slow response to the outbreak in its early stages may also have been the result of poor communication by officials.</p><p>Per <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/08/19/world/asia/china-coronavirus-beijing-trump.html\">a New York Times report in August</a>, US intelligence officials believe that local health officials in Wuhan originally underreported the severity of the coronavirus outbreak to officials in Beijing, probably because they feared being punished.</p><p>Health experts told CNN that the country had made mistakes in the early stages of the pandemic.</p><p>\"It was clear they did make mistakes -- and not just mistakes that happen when you're dealing with a novel virus -- also bureaucratic and politically-motivated errors in how they handled it,\" Yanzhong Huang, a senior fellow for global health at the Council on Foreign Relations, told CNN.</p><p>\"These had global consequences. You can never guarantee 100% transparency. It's not just about any intentional cover-up, you are also constrained with by technology and other issues with a novel virus. But even if they had been 100% transparent, that would not stop the Trump administration downplaying the seriousness of it. It would probably not have stopped this developing into a pandemic.\"</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
